## Acute Myeloid Leukemia

### Trials

### Trial: Randomized Phase III GVHD Prophylaxis in Haploidentical PBSC Transplantation

**Journal/Source:** Blood | **Date:** 2026-06-25 | **PMID:** 41849227 | **DOI:** 10.1182/blood.2025032569 | **NCT:** NCT03608059

**Disease/Setting:** Acute myeloid leukemia (AML) or myelodysplastic syndromes with excess blasts ≥II; haploidentical peripheral blood stem cell transplantation.

**Phase/Design:** Phase III, open-label, randomized (2:1:1); multicenter.

**N Enrolled:** 407 patients randomized (ATG/PTCy: 185; standard-dose ATG: 113; PTCy-only: 109).

**Population/Eligibility:** Ages 14–70 years with AML or MDS with excess blasts ≥II.

**Interventions:**
- **ATG/PTCy (n=185):** Low-dose ATG (5 mg/kg total) + posttransplant cyclophosphamide (50 mg/kg total)
- **Standard ATG (n=113):** High-dose ATG (10 mg/kg total)
- **PTCy-only (n=109):** PTCy (100 mg/kg total)

**Coprimary Endpoints & Results:**
1. **Cumulative incidence (CI) of grade 2–4 acute GVHD by day +100:** No significant difference among the 3 groups (P = .210).
2. **GVHD-free, relapse-free survival at 1 year:** not reported.

**Key Secondary Findings:**
- **Overall chronic GVHD incidence:** Comparable across all groups (P = .110).
- **2-year CI of moderate-to-severe chronic GVHD:** ATG/PTCy 17.4%, standard ATG 17.3%, PTCy-only 28.3%; difference did not reach statistical significance (P = .095).
- **Survival outcomes:** No significant differences among the 3 groups.
- **Neutrophil and platelet recovery:** Significantly higher in ATG/PTCy group than other groups (P < .001).

**Overall Survival:** Not explicitly reported as reached or immature.


**Title:** All-Oral Treatment of Newly Diagnosed Acute Myeloid Leukemia.

**Journal/Source:** The New England Journal of Medicine

**Date:** 2026-06-04

**PMID:** 42235013 | **DOI:** 10.1056/NEJMoa2510223 | **NCT:** NCT04657081

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Newly diagnosed acute myeloid leukemia; patients ≥75 years or ineligible for intensive induction chemotherapy.

**Phase/Design:** Phase 1-2, open-label, multicenter, nonrandomized trial.

**N Enrolled:** 189 total (30 phase 1, 58 phase 2a, 101 phase 2b pivotal).

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Newly diagnosed AML; age ≥75 or ineligible for intensive chemotherapy.

**Intervention vs Comparator:** Oral decitabine-cedazuridine plus oral venetoclax; no comparator (single-arm).

**Primary Endpoint + Result (Phase 1-2a):** Venetoclax area under the curve (0–24 h) and maximum observed concentration ± decitabine-cedazuridine (drug-interaction assessment) on days 5 and 15 of cycle 2. **Result:** No drug-drug interactions observed.

**Primary Endpoint + Result (Phase 2b, pivotal):** Complete response (CR). **Result:** 47% (95% CI, 36–57).

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**
- CR or CRi: 63% (95% CI, 53–73)
- **Overall survival:** Median 15.5 months (95% CI, 7.6 to not estimable). Status (mature/immature): not reported explicitly; confidence interval not yet bounded above suggests immature follow-up.
- Grade ≥3 adverse events in phase 2b: anemia 30%, neutropenia 26%, febrile neutropenia 25%.
- 30-day mortality: 3%; 60-day mortality: 10%.

**Total marrow and lymphoid irradiation in combination with cyclophosphamide and etoposide before haematopoietic cell transplantation for relapsed or refractory acute leukaemia: a single-centre, open-label, phase 2 trial**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | The Lancet. Haematology |
| Date | 2026-Jun |
| PMID | 42150590 |
| DOI | 10.1016/S2352-3026(26)00014-1 |
| NCT | NCT02094794 |
| **Disease/setting** | Relapsed or refractory acute myeloid leukaemia or acute lymphoblastic leukaemia; allogeneic HCT conditioning |
| **Phase** | Phase II |
| **Design** | Single-centre, open-label; initial 6-patient safety lead-in; 106 patients treated (out of 107 enrolled; 1 ineligible) |
| **Population** | Age 16–60 years; relapsed/refractory AML or ALL; sibling or matched/one-allele-mismatched unrelated donors |
| **Intervention** | Total marrow and lymphoid irradiation (TMLI) 2000 cGy to bone marrow and lymph nodes on days −9 to −5; etoposide 60 mg/kg on day −4; cyclophosphamide 100 mg/kg on day −2; bone marrow or peripheral blood stem cell infusion day 0; GVHD prophylaxis tacrolimus + sirolimus |
| **Comparator** | None; single-arm study |
| **Primary endpoint** | 2-year progression-free survival (safety lead-in: toxicity) |
| **Primary result** | 2-year PFS: 34% (95% CI 25–43%); all 106 treated patients included in analysis |
| **OS reported?** | Not reported as primary endpoint. Median follow-up 1.8 years (IQR 0.6–3.0) for all patients; 3.1 years (2.1–4.9) for patients alive at last contact. OS data not provided in abstract. |
| **Key secondary findings** | Grade 3–4 adverse events: cytopenias 96 (91%), metabolic disorders 83 (78%), oral mucositis 45 (42%), diarrhoea 25 (24%), nausea 21 (20%), palmar-plantar erythrodysesthesia 11 (10%). One treatment-related death (sinusoidal obstruction syndrome). No unacceptable toxicity in safety lead-in (n=6). |
| **Funding** | National Institutes of Health and Accuray |


**Cladribine With Low-Dose Cytarabine and Venetoclax Alternating With Azacitidine and Venetoclax for Newly Diagnosed Acute Myeloid Leukemia**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | American Journal of Hematology |
| Date | 2026-Jul |
| PMID | 42035228 |
| DOI | 10.1002/ajh.70328 |
| NCT | not reported |
| Disease / setting / line | Newly diagnosed AML; older or unfit patients |
| Phase | Phase II |
| Design | Single-arm; open-label |
| N enrolled | 190 |
| Median age | 68 years (range 47–84; 13% ≥75 years) |
| Risk stratification (ELN 2022) | Favorable 16%; intermediate 20%; adverse 64% |
| **Primary endpoint(s)** | CR/CRi rate; MRD-negative CR/CRi rate |
| **Primary result** | CR/CRi: 84% overall; 91% in TP53-WT AML. MRD-negative CR/CRi: 75% overall; 77% in TP53-WT AML |
| **Key secondary endpoints** | Overall survival (OS); event-free survival (EFS); early mortality; transplantation rate |
| **OS result** | Median OS 52 months; 2-year OS 60%; 5-year OS 45%. In MRD-negative CR: median OS not reached; 2-year OS 70% |
| **EFS result** | Median EFS 50 months; 2-year EFS 56%; 5-year EFS 43% |
| **Early mortality** | 4-week mortality 1%; 8-week mortality 3% |
| **Transplantation** | 44% of responders proceeded to allogeneic HSCT |
| **Follow-up duration** | Median follow-up duration not reported |

**Appraisal note:** Open-label, single-arm design with investigator-assessed remission endpoints. OS is reported and mature (median 52 months). No comparator arm; outcomes cannot be directly compared to standard alternatives.

**Title:** Imetelstat improves patient-reported outcomes and quality of life in lower-risk myelodysplastic syndromes: results from the phase III IMerge study.

**Journal/Source:** Haematologica | **Date:** 2026-Jul-01 | **PMID:** 41568521 | **DOI:** 10.3324/haematol.2025.288956 | **NCT:** NCT02598661

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Lower-risk MDS (LR-MDS) with RBC transfusion-dependent anemia; patients not responding to, having lost response to, or ineligible for erythropoiesis-stimulating agents

**Phase/Design/N:** Phase III, randomized controlled trial, multicenter; N not explicitly reported in abstract

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Adult patients with LR-MDS with RBC transfusion dependency and anemia

**Intervention vs. Comparator:** Imetelstat (telomerase inhibitor) vs. placebo

**Primary Endpoint + Result:** ≥8-week RBC transfusion independence (TI) — imetelstat resulted in clinically meaningful, statistically significant increases vs. placebo; exact response rate and HR/RR/95% CI not reported in abstract

**Key Secondary/Exploratory Endpoints:**
- Patient-reported outcomes (fatigue, quality of life): fewer imetelstat-treated patients experienced deterioration in fatigue; more experienced sustained improvement vs. placebo (nominal p-values reported; multiplicity adjustment not stated)
- RBC-TI responders at 8-week, 24-week, 1-year showed sustained improvements in fatigue thresholds (70%, 73%, 88% vs. 37%, 41%, 44% in non-responders; P<0.001, P=0.004, P=0.002) and QOL (43–53% vs. 21–30%; P≤0.0126)
- **Overall survival:** Not reported

**Note:** These are exploratory analyses within the pivotal IMerge trial; the primary phase III endpoint (RBC-TI) was previously published. This report focuses on patient-reported outcome stratifications.

## Myeloproliferative Neoplasms

### Guidelines

# Defining Remission and Relapse After Allogeneic Hematopoietic Cell Transplantation in Myelodysplastic/Myeloproliferative Neoplasms

**Journal:** Bone Marrow Transplantation  
**Date:** May 2026  
**PMID:** 41922738  
**DOI:** 10.1038/s41409-026-02843-y  
**Issuing body:** European Society for Blood and Marrow Transplantation (EBMT) Practice Harmonization & Guidelines Committee and Chronic Malignancies Working Party  

## Disease scope
Myelodysplastic/myeloproliferative neoplasms (excluding CMML); post-allogeneic hematopoietic cell transplantation (allo-HCT) settings.

## Key recommendations

**Remission criteria:** Proposed criteria for remission confirmation, including timing and thresholds for:
- Morphological assessment
- Molecular analysis
- Cytogenetic analysis
- Chimerism analysis

Aim: standardize response assessment and enable comparison in registry data and international series.

**Post-transplant surveillance and management:**
- Guidance for poor graft function and splenomegaly (aligned broadly with recommendations for myelofibrosis and related disorders)
- Recognition that relapse post-transplant remains frequent and lacks robust evidence base

## Evidence level
not reported (expert consensus-based).

## What is new/changed
not reported (document is presented as framework addressing previously unaddressed gaps in remission definition, post-transplant surveillance, and management of graft function and relapse in this rare disease group).

## Clinical context
Myelodysplastic/myeloproliferative neoplasms (excluding CMML) account for <1% of allo-HCT procedures in Europe annually. Allo-HCT is currently the only curative therapy. Experience is limited by rarity; response assessment, post-transplant surveillance, and management of complications are not well established.

### Trials

## Phase 2 study of bomedemstat for essential thrombocythemia

**Journal:** Blood Advances  
**Publication date:** 2026-May-26  
**PMID:** 41758981  
**DOI:** 10.1182/bloodadvances.2025017575  
**NCT:** NCT04254978

**Disease/setting:** Essential thrombocythemia (ET), second-line or later cytoreduction (inadequate response or intolerance to ≥1 standard therapy)

**Phase/design:** Phase II, open-label, single-arm, multicenter  
**N enrolled:** 73

**Population:** Participants with ET requiring cytoreduction; had inadequate response to or were intolerant of ≥1 standard therapy

**Intervention:** Bomedemstat (lysine-specific demethylase 1 inhibitor), starting dose 0.6 mg/kg per day, titrated to target platelet count 200–400 × 10⁹/L

**Primary endpoints:**  
- Safety and response (defined as platelet count ≤400 × 10⁹/L without new thromboembolic events)  
- At 24 weeks: 49 of 64 evaluable participants (77%) achieved response

**Key secondary/supporting outcomes:**  
- Durable platelet reduction (≤400 × 10⁹/L for ≥12 weeks): 52 of 72 (72%)  
- Durable WBC reduction (<10 × 10⁹/L for ≥12 weeks): 61 of 72 (85%)  
- Of 10 with elevated WBC at baseline, 9 had normal WBC at week 24  
- Hemoglobin: remained stable  
- VAF reduction (CALR, JAK2, or MPL) at week 24: 39 of 46 evaluable (85%)  
- Thrombotic events by week 24: 2 of 73 (3%)  
- Hemorrhagic events by week 24: 15 of 73 (21%)  
- Grade 3 or 4 AEs (overall treatment period): 34 of 73 (47%)  
- Treatment interruption: 29 of 73 (40%)  
- Permanent discontinuation: 11 of 73 (15%)  
- Treatment-related deaths: 0

**OS/event-free survival:** Not reported

**Funding/sponsorship:** Not reported in abstract

### PETALs trial – Nilotinib ± pegylated interferon alfa-2a in newly diagnosed CP-CML

**Journal:** The Lancet. Haematology | **Publication date:** May 2026 | **PMID:** 42069411 | **DOI:** 10.1016/S2352-3026(26)00043-8 | **NCT:** NCT02201459

**Disease setting:** Chronic phase chronic myeloid leukaemia (CML), newly diagnosed, first-line therapy, France (27 academic centres)

**Phase:** III | **Design:** Open-label, randomized, multicentre; 1:1 allocation; stratified by Sokal index and European Treatment and Outcome Study long-term survival index | **N enrolled:** 205 (5 ineligible, 200 intent-to-treat); 99 nilotinib monotherapy, 101 combination

**Population:** Age 18–65 years, Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group performance score ≤2, major BCR::ABL1 transcripts, no prior TKI exposure; median age 45 years (IQR 36–55); 65% male

**Intervention vs comparator:**
- Nilotinib monotherapy: 300 mg oral twice daily
- Nilotinib + pegylated interferon alfa-2a: 300 mg nilotinib twice daily + subcutaneous Peg-IFN 30 µg/week for month 1, then 45 µg/week for maximum 2 years

**Primary endpoint:** Cumulative rate of MR4.5 (BCR::ABL1 IS ≤0.0032%) at month 12
- **Result:** Combination 24% (95% CI 16.0–34.1) vs nilotinib 15% (8.6–24.2); p = 0.048
- **Overall survival:** Not reported as primary endpoint; median follow-up 67 months (IQR 32.6–70.6) but OS status/maturity not stated

**Key secondary endpoints:** not reported

**Safety:**
- Grade 3–4 haematological toxicity: 14 patients per group
- Grade 3–4 thrombocytopenia: 6 (combination) vs 5 (nilotinib), no haemorrhages reported
- Grade 3–4 psychiatric events: 6 patients (6%, combination) including 3 unsuccessful suicide attempts vs 5 patients (5%, nilotinib) including 1 unsuccessful suicide attempt
- Vascular events (all grade 3–4): 6 events in 6 patients (combination) vs 7 events in 5 patients (nilotinib)

**Interpretation (per abstract):** Combination therapy achieved higher initial MR4.5 rates but with additional toxicity, particularly psychiatric adverse events. Authors note that whether early molecular response translates to sustained treatment-free remission requires a randomized trial powered for that outcome.

**Funding:** Novartis Pharma

### Phase II trial: Ropeginterferon alfa-2b for prefibrotic and lower-risk myelofibrosis

**Journal:** Blood Advances | **Date:** 2026-06-09 | **PMID:** 41875235 | **DOI:** 10.1182/bloodadvances.2026019612 | **NCT:** NCT04988815

**Disease/setting/line:** Prefibrotic primary MF (pre-PMF) and Dynamic International Prognostic Scoring System low-/intermediate-1-risk fibrotic primary MF or secondary MF; patients requiring cytoreduction, previously on hydroxyurea.

**Phase/design/N:** Phase II, open-label, single-arm. N = 71 enrolled (40 men, 31 women); median age 60 years (range 31–86); followed up median 119 weeks (range 10–131).

**Population/eligibility:** Pre-PMF or fibrotic MF (primary or secondary) with low-/intermediate-1 risk score; indication for cytoreduction; eligible to switch from hydroxyurea.

**Intervention:** Ropeginterferon alfa-2b (ropeg), a monopegylated interferon alfa-2b. Dosing: week 0: 250 μg; week 2: 350 μg; week 4 onward: 500 μg every 2 weeks (replacing hydroxyurea).

**Comparator:** None (single-arm).

**Primary endpoints:** Safety and clinicohematologic complete response (CHCR).

**Primary endpoint results:**
- **CHCR at week 24:** 63.8% overall (pre-PMF 74%, fibrotic PMF 20%, fibrotic SMF 42.9%)
- **CHCR at week 48:** 63.5% overall (pre-PMF 69.6%, fibrotic PMF 25%, SMF 53.9%)
- **CHCR at week 104:** 70% overall (pre-PMF 78.4%, fibrotic PMF 33.3%, SMF 50%)
- **Safety:** 3 treatment discontinuations (4.2%) due to adverse events. Thrombo-hemorrhagic events not observed after stopping hydroxyurea.

**Key secondary endpoints:**
- **JAK2V617F variant allele frequency (VAF) reduction:** week 24 53.1%, week 48 70%, week 104 67.6%
- **CALR mutant VAF reduction:** week 24 52.6%, week 48 42.9%, week 104 40%
- **Bone marrow reticulin fibrosis reduction (50 evaluable at week 104):** 13/50 (26%)

**Overall survival:** not reported.

**ASC4OPT: Asciminib Treatment Optimization in CML-CP After ≥2 TKI Failures**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | Leukemia |
| Publication date | Jun 2026 |
| PMID | 42026180 |
| DOI | 10.1038/s41375-026-02965-8 |
| NCT | NCT04948333 |
| **Phase & design** | Phase 3b, non-comparative, open-label, multicenter |
| **N enrolled** | 169 patients (139 not in MMR at baseline; 30 intolerant but in MMR at baseline) |
| **Disease/setting** | CML in chronic phase (CML-CP), previously treated with ≥2 TKIs, with unsatisfactory response (intolerance, warning, or failure per ELN 2020 criteria) or intolerance with baseline MMR |
| **Intervention** | Asciminib: 40 mg BID or 80 mg QD; dose escalation to 200 mg QD available in 40 patients |
| **Comparator** | None (non-comparative) |
| **Primary endpoint** | Major molecular response (MMR) rate at Week 48 in patients not in MMR at baseline |
| **Primary result** | **Week 48 MMR rate: 39.4% overall** (40 mg BID: 43.4%; 80 mg QD: 35.4%); **Week 96 MMR rate: 43.6% overall** (40 mg BID: 45.8%; 80 mg QD: 41.5%) |
| **Secondary endpoints** | MMR maintenance in baseline-MMR cohort; dose-escalation response |
| **Key secondary results** | Among 30 patients in MMR at baseline: 93.3% remained in MMR at Week 48, 86.7% at Week 96. Among 40 who escalated to 200 mg QD: 17.5% achieved MMR at Week 96 |
| **OS reported?** | No; not stated in abstract |
| **Safety** | Consistent with previous asciminib studies; specific adverse event rates not reported |
| **Conclusion (per authors)** | Asciminib supports consideration as a potential standard of care for CML-CP patients with suboptimal response to prior TKI therapy |

## Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia

### Trials

**FLAIR Trial: Patient-Reported Health-Related Quality of Life in Previously Untreated CLL**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Title** | Patient-reported health-related quality of life in previously untreated chronic lymphocytic leukaemia: Results from the randomised phase 3 FLAIR trial comparing ibrutinib-rituximab versus fludarabine-cyclophosphamide-rituximab |
| **Journal** | British Journal of Haematology |
| **Publication date** | May 2026 |
| **PMID** | 41912408 |
| **DOI** | 10.1111/bjh.70416 |
| **Disease / setting / line** | Previously untreated CLL; first-line |
| **Phase** | Phase III |
| **Design** | Randomized, open-label, multicenter (101 hospitals), comparative |
| **N enrolled** | Not reported in abstract |
| **Population / key eligibility** | Age 18–75 years; WHO PS ≤2; requiring treatment; excluded if >20% 17p deletion |
| **Intervention** | Ibrutinib + rituximab (IR), administered up to 6 years |
| **Comparator** | Fludarabine + cyclophosphamide + rituximab (FCR), 6 cycles |
| **Primary endpoint (from parent trial)** | Progression-free survival — improved with IR vs FCR (exact HR/p-value not stated in this QoL report) |
| **Secondary endpoints reported (this publication)** | Health-related quality of life (HR-QoL) via EORTC-QLQ-C30, QLQ-CLL16, EQ-5D-3L, EQ-VAS; function and symptom trajectories analyzed by repeated-measures multilevel regression |
| **Key results — HR-QoL** | HR-QoL trajectories were similar between arms. FCR recipients had worse scores at end of treatment but recovered thereafter. By 48 months, more FCR-treated participants showed meaningful improvements in several scales. Statistically significant differences (p < 0.05) favoured IR for physical, role, and social function; emotional function favoured FCR. Diarrhoea was more common with IR; fatigue and dyspnoea more common with FCR — differences did not exceed minimally important thresholds. Overall, scales were comparable between treatment groups; continuous IR does not compromise HR-QoL. |
| **Overall survival reported / mature** | Not reported in this publication |
| **Baseline compliance** | 84.4% completed baseline questionnaires; subsequent compliance 67.6%–83.5% |
| **Participant demographics (abstract)** | Median age 63 years; majority white and male |


## Phase III Trial: Venetoclax combinations in untreated CLL

**Title:** Venetoclax combinations in untreated CLL: 5-year results and patient-reported outcomes analysis of the CLL13/GAIA trial.

**Journal:** Blood | **Date:** 2026-Jun-18 | **PMID:** 41911073 | **DOI:** 10.1182/blood.2025032160 | **NCT:** NCT02950051

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Chronic lymphocytic leukemia (CLL), untreated, first-line, fit patients without TP53 aberrations.

**Phase:** Phase III | **Design:** Randomized controlled trial, multicenter. Four arms, comparator is chemoimmunotherapy (CIT).

**N enrolled:** 926 patients total (GIV: 231, GV: 229, RV: 237, CIT: 229 [FCR: 150, BR: 79]).

**Population:** Fit patients with untreated CLL without TP53 aberrations.

**Interventions:**
- **GIV (venetoclax-obinutuzumab-ibrutinib):** 12 cycles obinutuzumab-venetoclax, ibrutinib continuation until cycle 36 if MRD-positive at months 12/15.
- **GV (venetoclax-obinutuzumab):** 12 cycles venetoclax-obinutuzumab.
- **RV (venetoclax-rituximab):** 12 cycles venetoclax-rituximab.
- **Comparator CIT:** 6 cycles FCR (fludarabine-cyclophosphamide-rituximab, n=150) or BR (bendamustine-rituximab, n=79).

**Primary endpoint — Progression-free survival (PFS) at 5 years:**
- **GIV:** 81.3%
- **GV:** 69.8%
- **RV:** 57.4%
- **CIT:** 50.7%
- **Comparisons:** GV and GIV superior to CIT and RV (P < 0.001 each). GIV superior to GV (P = 0.0046).

**Overall survival (5-year rates, not reported as statistically discriminatory):**
- **GIV:** 94.3%
- **GV:** 93.6%
- **RV:** 94.7%
- **CIT:** 90.7%
- No differences in OS between treatment arms (stated).

**Key secondary endpoints:**
- **Treatment-free survival (2-year) after venetoclax-based re-treatment:** >80% from second-line treatment in venetoclax-pretreated patients.
- **Severe infections:** Highest incidence with CIT.
- **Cardiac events:** Most frequent with GIV.
- **Quality of life (QoL):** GV and RV reported rapid and significantly greater QoL improvements vs CIT. GIV reported clinically relevant QoL improvements later (month 15, post-treatment) due to higher treatment-related symptom burden.

**Median follow-up:** 63.8 months.

**Key observations:**
- Median observation time is robust (5-year data).
- OS mature but shows no significant difference between arms despite PFS divergence.
- Toxicity profile differs (infections vs cardiac events by arm).
- Patient-reported outcomes stratified by treatment arm; QoL trajectory varies.


### CRISTALLO Phase III Trial: Fixed-duration VenO vs FCR/BR in Treatment-Naïve CLL

**Title:** Fixed-duration VenO vs FCR/BR in fit patients with untreated CLL: primary analysis of the phase 3 CRISTALLO trial.

**Journal:** Blood | **Date:** 2026-Jun-11 | **PMID:** 41770817 | **DOI:** 10.1182/blood.2025030630 | **NCT:** NCT04285567

**Disease/Setting:** Chronic lymphocytic leukemia (CLL), first-line treatment, treatment-naïve, fit patients (CIRS ≤6, CrCl ≥70 mL/min) without del(17p)/TP53 mutations.

**Phase/Design:** Phase III, randomized, controlled trial, 1:1 allocation; Tier 1 journal (Blood); no mention of blinding status in abstract.

**N Enrolled:** 166 total (80 VenO; 86 FCR/BR); data cutoff 19 March 2024.

**Intervention vs Comparator:**
- **VenO:** Venetoclax-obinutuzumab, fixed-duration
- **FCR/BR:** Fludarabine-cyclophosphamide-rituximab OR bendamustine-rituximab (choice per institutional standard)

**Primary Endpoint & Result:**
Undetectable minimal residual disease (uMRD, <10⁻⁴) in peripheral blood (PB) at month 15 measured by next-generation sequencing.
- **VenO:** 81.3% (65/80)
- **FCR/BR:** 54.7% (47/86)
- **P = 0.0004** — primary endpoint met in favor of VenO.

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**
- **uMRD (<10⁻⁴) in PB and bone marrow (BM) at end of treatment:** higher with VenO vs FCR/BR (exact proportions not reported in abstract).
- **uMRD at deeper cutoff (<10⁻⁶) in PB at month 15:**
  - VenO: 65.0% (52/80)
  - FCR/BR: 25.6% (22/86)
- **Progression-free survival (PFS):** not evaluable at first interim analysis due to short follow-up. Events reported: 7 progressions/deaths (VenO) vs 13 (FCR/BR).
- **Overall survival (OS):** not reported.

**Safety:**
Consistent with known profiles of each drug; no high-risk tumor lysis syndrome (TLS) cases identified by obinutuzumab debulking; no clinical TLS occurred.

**Baseline Characteristics:** Generally balanced across arms.

---

**Appraisal:**
- Primary endpoint is a surrogate (uMRD); OS immature or not reported.
- Follow-up short at first interim analysis; PFS not yet evaluable.
- Compares to historical comparator (chemoimmunotherapy) rather than newer targeted agents; consistent with prior GAIA-CLL13 findings.
- Blinding status not reported in abstract.

**Title:** Final phase 2 study results of acalabrutinib in treatment-naive and relapsed/refractory chronic lymphocytic leukemia.  
**Journal/Source:** Blood Advances  
**Date:** 2026-Jun-09  
**PMID:** 41915892  
**DOI:** 10.1182/bloodadvances.2025018310  
**NCT:** NCT02029443  

**Disease/Setting/Line of Therapy:** CLL/SLL; treatment-naive (TN) and relapsed/refractory (R/R).  

**Phase/Design/N:** Phase 1/2 (long-term final analysis); single-arm; N = 99 TN, 134 R/R.  

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Patients with treatment-naive and relapsed/refractory CLL/SLL. Standard and high-risk genomic features represented.  

**Intervention:** Acalabrutinib monotherapy (selective, covalent BTK inhibitor).  

**Comparator:** None (single-arm study).  

**Primary Endpoint + Result:** Not explicitly stated; efficacy reported as overall response rate (ORR) and progression-free survival (PFS).  
- **ORR:** 97.0% (TN) and 94.8% (R/R).  
- **PFS (TN):** Median not reached; 72-month PFS rate 86.7% (95% CI, 77.0–92.5).  
- **PFS (R/R):** Median PFS 66.1 months (range 0.4–87.8); 72-month PFS rate 45.1% (95% CI, 35.6–54.1).  

**Key Secondary Endpoints/Safety:** Overall survival reported = not reported.  
- **Atrial fibrillation (any grade):** 6.1% (TN), 9.0% (R/R).  
- **Hypertension (any grade):** 29.3% (TN), 23.1% (R/R).  
- **Other malignancies (excluding nonmelanoma skin cancer, any grade):** 14.1% (TN), 17.2% (R/R).  
- **Major bleeding (any grade):** 8.1% (TN), 8.2% (R/R).  
- Incidence of most common adverse events decreased over time.  
- Median follow-up: 73.7 months (TN), 52.6 months (R/R).  
- Patients remaining on treatment at final cutoff: 71% (TN), 31% (R/R).  

**Notes:** Final analysis of a long-term phase 1/2 study. No new safety signals with extended follow-up.

### Duvelisib + venetoclax in R/R CLL/SLL and Richter transformation

**Journal/Source:** Blood Advances  
**Publication Date:** 2026-06-09  
**PMID:** 41886642  
**DOI:** 10.1182/bloodadvances.2025018878  
**NCT:** NCT03534323

**Disease/Setting:** Relapsed/refractory CLL/SLL (n=35) and Richter transformation (n=9); R/R population with median 2 prior therapies, 60% prior BTKi, 46% TP53 aberrant

**Phase/Design:** Phase 1/2; open-label; sequential dose escalation (phase 1) then expansion (phase 2); no concurrent comparator arm

**Intervention:** Duvelisib (PI3K inhibitor) 25 mg twice daily + venetoclax 400 mg daily (started after 1 week duvelisib); patients achieving CR with uMRD at 1 year could discontinue; those with detectable MRD continued venetoclax monotherapy until 2 separate uMRD assessments

**Primary Endpoints & Results:**  
- Best overall response rate (ORR): 91% (exact CI not reported)  
- Best complete response (CR) rate: 60% (exact CI not reported)  
- Peripheral blood uMRD at 10⁻⁴ (cycle 13): 43%  
- Bone marrow uMRD at 10⁻⁴ (cycle 13): 40%  

**Key Secondary/Efficacy Endpoints:**  
- Median progression-free survival (PFS) for CLL/SLL: 46 months  
- 3-year PFS: 67% (95% CI 0.51–0.86)  
- Overall survival: not reported  
- Richter transformation subset (n=9): 4 patients achieved response, 3 CRs; details sparse

**Safety:**  
- Neutropenia (grade ≥3): 91%  
- Febrile neutropenia: 6%  
- Diarrhea: 63% (grade ≥3: 14%)  
- Elevated aspartate aminotransferase: 51% (grade ≥3: 9%)  
- Serious adverse events and immune-mediated toxicities noted; specific rates not detailed in abstract

**Maximum Tolerated Dose:** Not reached in phase 1

### DLBCL — Phase III Trial

**Tucidinostat Plus R-CHOP vs R-CHOP in MYC/BCL2 Double-Expressor DLBCL**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | JAMA |
| Publication date | 2026-05-19 |
| PMID | 42018318 |
| DOI | 10.1001/jama.2026.4199 |
| NCT | NCT04231448 |
| **Disease** | DLBCL with MYC/BCL2 coexpression (double-expressor lymphoma); first-line treatment |
| **Design** | Randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled, phase III; 40 centers in China |
| **N enrolled** | 423 (median age 63 years; 47.5% male) |
| **Follow-up** | Median 41.3 months from randomization |
| **Intervention** | Tucidinostat 20 mg on days 1, 4, 8, 11 of each 21-day cycle × 6 cycles plus R-CHOP; responders received maintenance tucidinostat or placebo up to 24 weeks |
| **Comparator** | Matching placebo plus 6 cycles of R-CHOP; responders received placebo maintenance |
| **Primary endpoint** | Event-free survival (freedom from progression, relapse, death, or initiation of new therapy for residual disease) |
| **Primary result** | **Stratified HR 0.72 (95% CI 0.54–0.96; p = 0.02)** — tucidinostat group had 28% lower risk of event. 2-year EFS: 60.3% vs 50.5% (placebo). |
| **Secondary endpoints** | Complete response rate: 73.0% (tucidinostat) vs 61.8% (placebo; difference 11.1%, 95% CI 2.3–20.0%). Progression-free survival, disease-free survival, and overall survival reported as secondary outcomes. Overall survival not yet mature per abstract. |
| **Safety** | Increased toxicity in tucidinostat group; described as "generally manageable with supportive care." Specific adverse events not detailed in abstract. |
| **Conclusions** | Tucidinostat plus R-CHOP significantly improved event-free survival with manageable toxicity in newly diagnosed MYC/BCL2 double-expressor DLBCL. Described as first epigenetic modulator demonstrated to benefit DLBCL. |

## Ten-Year Outcomes after CAR T-Cell Therapy for B-Cell Lymphomas

**Journal:** The New England Journal of Medicine  
**Date:** 2026-06-25  
**PMID:** 42341302  
**DOI:** 10.1056/NEJMoa2518035  
**NCT:** NCT02030834  

**Disease/Setting:** Relapsed or refractory B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphomas (DLBCL and follicular lymphoma)

**Phase/Design:** Phase II, single-arm, long-term follow-up study (10.1 years median, range 7.9–11.5)

**N enrolled:** 38 patients total (24 DLBCL, 14 follicular lymphoma)

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Patients with relapsed or refractory B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphomas (heavily pretreated) who received tisagenlecleucel (CTL019)

**Intervention:** Single infusion of autologous anti-CD19 CAR T cells (tisagenlecleucel) with 4-1BB costimulation

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary Endpoint — Lymphoma-Free Survival (LFS) at 10 years:**
- DLBCL: 32% (95% CI, 14–51); no relapses beyond 5.4 years
- Follicular lymphoma: 47% (95% CI, 20–71)

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**
- 10-year progression-free survival (PFS) including deaths from any cause:
  - DLBCL: 17% (95% CI, 5–34)
  - Follicular lymphoma: 29% (95% CI, 9–52)
- 10-year overall survival (OS):
  - DLBCL: 17% (95% CI, 5–34)
  - Follicular lymphoma: 50% (95% CI, 23–72)
- 10-year non-relapse-related mortality: 18% overall (14% excluding COVID-19–related deaths)
- 10-year cumulative incidence of second primary cancer: 21% (9 patients)
- Persistent grade 2–3 neutropenia: 5% (2 patients); no late anemia or thrombocytopenia
- CAR-transgene persistence associated with long-term response; B-cell aplasia persisted in 44% of responders

**Data-cutoff:** October 1, 2025

## Tafasitamab plus lenalidomide and R-CHOP versus R-CHOP for first-line treatment of high-risk DLBCL (frontMIND)

**Journal/Source:** Lancet (London, England)  
**Publication Date:** 2026-06-20  
**PMID:** 42217458  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S0140-6736(26)00866-4  
**NCT:** not reported  

### Trial Details

**Disease/Setting/Line:** High-intermediate-risk or high-risk diffuse large B-cell lymphoma (DLBCL) or high-grade B-cell lymphoma (HGBL); first-line treatment  
**Phase:** Phase III  
**Design:** Randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled, multicenter (298 centres across North America, South America, Europe, Asia-Pacific)  
**N Enrolled:** 899 patients (448 tafa-len-R-CHOP; 451 R-CHOP)  

### Population

Previously untreated patients aged 18–80 years with high-intermediate-risk or high-risk DLBCL or HGBL. Stratified by International Prognostic Index (IPI) or age-adjusted IPI and geographical region.  

### Intervention vs Comparator

**Experimental:** Six 21-day cycles of tafasitamab (Fc-enhanced anti-CD19 monoclonal antibody) plus lenalidomide plus R-CHOP (rituximab, cyclophosphamide, doxorubicin, vincristine, prednisone/prednisolone)  
**Comparator:** Standard six 21-day cycles of R-CHOP  

### Primary Endpoint & Result

**Progression-free survival (PFS):** 
- HR 0.75 (95% CI 0.59–0.96); p = 0.0194
- 2-year PFS: 71.1% (95% CI 66.3–75.4) with tafa-len-R-CHOP vs 62.9% (95% CI 57.9–67.5) with R-CHOP

### Key Secondary Endpoints

**Overall Survival (interim):**  
HR 0.85 (95% CI 0.63–1.14) — **OS data are immature**; median follow-up 35.2 months (95% CI 35.0–35.4).  
Total deaths: 82 (19%) in tafa-len-R-CHOP group vs 97 (22%) in R-CHOP group.  

**Safety:**
- Grade 3 or higher treatment-emergent adverse events: 87% (384/443) with tafa-len-R-CHOP vs 76% (340/447) with R-CHOP
- Fatal treatment-emergent adverse events: 6% (26) with tafa-len-R-CHOP vs 4% (17) with R-CHOP
- Premature discontinuation of all study drugs: 16% (71/443) tafa-len-R-CHOP vs 15% (66/447) R-CHOP

### Funding

Incyte Corporation (sponsor of tafasitamab)  

### Interpretation (per authors)

Progression-free survival significantly improved with tafa-len-R-CHOP; however, safety profile shows increases in adverse events, including treatment-related deaths. Overall survival data immature; follow-up ongoing. Further analyses (circulating tumor DNA) needed.

**EPCORE DLBCL-3: Epcoritamab monotherapy vs epcoritamab + lenalidomide for newly diagnosed DLBCL**

| **NCT** | NCT05660967 |
| **Disease/setting** | Newly diagnosed CD20+ large B-cell lymphoma (DLBCL), Ann Arbor stage II–IV; patients ≥80 years or ≥75 with significant comorbidities (ineligible for anthracycline-based chemoimmunotherapy) |
| **Phase** | 2 |
| **Design** | Open-label, multicentre, randomised; stage 1 (n=44 per arm) followed by stage 2 expansion of selected arm based on stage 1 results |
| **N enrolled / treated** | 108 treated (stage 1: 44 epcoritamab monotherapy, 44 epcoritamab + lenalidomide, 2 not treated; stage 2: 22 enrolled in selected arm, 1 not treated) |

| **Intervention** | **Epcoritamab monotherapy:** step-up dosing (0.16 mg day 1, 0.08 mg day 8 of cycle 1), then 48 mg SC weekly for cycles 1–3, then 48 mg Q4W for cycles 4–12 (up to 12 cycles). **Epcoritamab + lenalidomide:** same epcoritamab schedule + lenalidomide 10 or 20 mg PO daily days 1–21 of each 28-day cycle, up to 12 cycles |
| **Comparator** | Epcoritamab monotherapy vs epcoritamab + lenalidomide |

Stage 2 (monotherapy only): 45.5% (95% CI 24.4–67.8; n=10/22). Combined stages 1–2 (monotherapy only): 57.6% (95% CI 44.8–69.7; n=38/66). |
| **Key secondary endpoints** | Overall survival: **not reported.** | Disease progression, event-free survival, safety. |
| **Safety (Grade ≥3 AE)** | **Stage 1 epcoritamab monotherapy (n=44):** infections 18%, fatigue 14%; serious AE in 64%. Treatment-emergent deaths: 6 (14%) — cytomegalovirus reactivation, COVID-19 pneumonia, SARS-CoV-2, tumour lysis syndrome, neuroendocrine lung tumour, tumour haemorrhage. **Stage 1 epcoritamab + lenalidomide (n=42):** neutropenia 40%, infections 38%; serious AE in 81%. Deaths: 6 (14%) — pneumonia, COVID-19, sepsis, general health deterioration, MOD, acute cardiac failure. **All epcoritamab monotherapy patients (stages 1–2, n=66):** infections 24%, neutropenia 12%, hypertension 11%; serious AE in 70%. Stage 2 deaths: 2 (3%) — MOD, acute respiratory failure. |
| **Arm selection** | Based on stage 1 CR rate and safety profile, epcoritamab monotherapy selected for stage 2 expansion. |
| **Funding** | Genmab and AbbVie. |

**Title:** Ten-Year Outcomes after CAR T-Cell Therapy for B-Cell Lymphomas

**Journal/source:** The New England Journal of Medicine

**Date:** 2026-06-25

**PMID:** 42341302

**DOI:** 10.1056/NEJMoa2518035

**NCT:** NCT02030834

**Disease/setting/line:** Relapsed or refractory B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma (24 with large B-cell lymphoma, 14 with follicular lymphoma); heavily pretreated population

**Phase:** Phase II

**Design:** Single-arm, open-label; patients evaluated for long-term outcomes following a single infusion of tisagenlecleucel (anti-CD19 CAR T-cell therapy)

**N enrolled:** 38 (14 with follicular lymphoma)

**Population/key eligibility:** Patients with relapsed or refractory B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma; age and prior therapy status not fully specified in abstract

**Intervention:** CTL019 / tisagenlecleucel — autologous T cells expressing CD19-directed, 4-1BB-costimulated chimeric antigen receptors; single infusion

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary endpoint and result:**
- **Lymphoma-free survival** (time from infusion to relapse or lymphoma-related death) at 10 years:
  - Follicular lymphoma: 47% (95% CI, 20–71)
  - Large B-cell lymphoma: 32% (95% CI, 14–51)
  - No relapses occurred beyond 5.4 years

**Key secondary endpoints and results:**
- **10-year progression-free survival** (deaths from any cause included):
  - Follicular lymphoma: 29% (95% CI, 9–52)
  - Large B-cell lymphoma: 17% (95% CI, 5–34)
- **10-year overall survival:**
  - Follicular lymphoma: 50% (95% CI, 23–72)
  - Large B-cell lymphoma: 17% (95% CI, 5–34)
- **Toxicity:** Grade 2–3 persistent neutropenia in 2 patients (5%); no late anemia or thrombocytopenia
- **Second primary cancer:** 9 patients (10-year cumulative incidence, 21%)
- **Non-relapse-related mortality:** 18% at 10 years (14% when COVID-19 deaths excluded)
- **CAR-transgene persistence:** Associated with long-term response; B-cell aplasia persisted in 44% of responders

**OS reported:** Yes, at 10 years (see above)

**Median follow-up:** 10.1 years (range, 7.9–11.5); data cutoff 2025-10-01

**Title:** Lenalidomide plus rituximab for previously untreated advanced follicular lymphoma: the 10-year RELEVANCE trial analysis.

**Journal/Source:** Blood | 2026-Jun-18

**PMID:** 41915772 | **DOI:** 10.1182/blood.2026033126 | **NCT:** NCT01476787, NCT01650701

**Disease/Setting:** Previously untreated advanced follicular lymphoma, first-line therapy.

**Phase/Design:** Phase III, multinational, randomized controlled trial (open-label). Comparator: rituximab-based immunochemotherapy (R-Chemo).

**N Enrolled:** 1030 (R2, n=513; R-Chemo, n=517).

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Previously untreated, advanced follicular lymphoma (not specified further in abstract).

**Intervention vs Comparator:**
- Intervention: Rituximab + lenalidomide (R2)
- Comparator: Rituximab-based immunochemotherapy (R-Chemo)

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**
Progression-free survival (PFS, independent review committee assessment) at 120 months:
- Median PFS: 110.6 months (R2) vs 102.8 months (R-Chemo)
- 10-year PFS rates: 46.4% (R2) vs 46.6% (R-Chemo)
- No formal p-value reported for PFS difference; point estimate suggests non-inferiority of R2 but no superiority.

**Key Secondary Endpoints + Results:**
- Overall survival (OS): Median OS not reached in either arm. 10-year OS rates: 82.4% (R2) vs 81.1% (R-Chemo). OS was reported but not formally tested for difference between arms.
- Time-to-next lymphoma treatment (TTNLT): Median not reached; 10-year rates: 62.2% (R2) vs 66.3% (R-Chemo).
- Progression of disease within 24 months (POD24): hazard ratio 6.215 (95% CI not reported), p<0.0001; no difference between study groups.
- Second primary malignancies (SPMs): 2.11 cases per 100 patient-years (95% CI 1.80–2.46).
- Transformations after 24 months: 9 total (3 R2 vs 6 R-Chemo).
- Deaths: 87 in each group, primarily from lymphoma progression and SPMs.

**Conclusion:** R2 confirmed as a chemotherapy-free alternative to immunochemotherapy in previously untreated follicular lymphoma, based on comparable long-term PFS and OS.

## Mantle Cell Lymphoma

### Trials

**TRIANGLE (3-arm, phase 3, European MCL Network)**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Title | Addition of autologous stem-cell transplantation to an ibrutinib-containing first-line treatment in patients aged 18-65 years with mantle cell lymphoma (TRIANGLE): 4·5-year follow-up of a three-arm, randomised, open-label, phase 3 superiority trial of the European MCL Network |
| Journal | Lancet (London, England) |
| Date | 2026-May-16 |
| PMID | 42134356 |
| DOI | 10.1016/S0140-6736(26)00362-4 |
| NCT | not reported |
| **Disease / setting** | Untreated, stage II–IV mantle cell lymphoma; patients aged 18–65 years, eligible for ASCT; 13 European countries and Israel |
| **Phase / design** | Phase 3, three-arm, randomised, open-label, superiority trial; 165 secondary/tertiary centres |
| **N enrolled** | 870 patients (662 [76%] male, 208 [24%] female); group A (n=288), group A+I (n=292), group I (n=290) |
| **Intervention vs comparator** | Group A: R-CHOP × 6 cycles (21-day). Group A+I: R-CHOP + ibrutinib + R-DHAP/R-DHAOx + ibrutinib maintenance 2 years. Group I: ibrutinib + R-DHAP/R-DHAOx + ibrutinib maintenance 2 years |
| **Primary endpoint + result** | Failure-free survival (modified form of PFS) at 4 years. A+I vs I: 82% (95% CI 78–87) vs 81% (76–86); HR 0.86 (one-sided 98.33% CI 0.00–1.27); one-sided p=0.21 (A+I did NOT show superiority over I). A+I vs A: 82% (78–87) vs 70% (65–76); HR 0.63 (one-sided 98.33% CI 0.00–0.89); one-sided p=0.0026 (A+I superior to A). I vs A: 81% (76–86) vs 70% (65–76); HR 1.45 (one-sided 98.33% CI 0.00–2.02); one-sided p=0.99 (I did NOT show superiority over A). |
| **Overall survival (reported)** | 4-year OS: A+I 88% (95% CI 84–92) vs A 81% (76–85), HR 0.59 (95% CI 0.38–0.92), p=0.0036. I 90% (87–94) vs A 81% (76–85), HR 0.57 (95% CI 0.36–0.90), p=0.0019. |
| **Key secondary endpoints** | Grade 3–5 adverse events during maintenance/follow-up: haematological disorders in A+I 127/234 (54%) vs I 74/269 (28%) vs A 56/240 (23%); infections in A+I 80/234 (34%) vs I 71/269 (26%) vs A 37/240 (15%). Fatal adverse events (infections/infestations) in A+I 4/234 (2%) and I 5/269 (2%). |
| **Median follow-up** | 54.9 months (95% CI 54.4–56.0) |
| **Interpretation** | Both ibrutinib-containing groups (A+I and I) showed improvement in both failure-free survival and overall survival vs control (A). Addition of ASCT to ibrutinib-containing regimen (A+I) conferred no added benefit over ibrutinib alone (I) in failure-free survival but increased toxicity (higher rates of haematological toxicity and infections). Ibrutinib + R-CHOP/R-DHAP + 2-year ibrutinib maintenance recommended as new standard for younger MCL patients. |
| **Funding** | Janssen |

## Hodgkin Lymphoma

### Guidelines

**Title:** Autologous and allogeneic haematopoietic cell transplantation in adult patients with Hodgkin lymphoma: recommendations from the EBMT Practice Harmonisation and Guidelines Committee and Lymphoma Working Party.

**Source:** The Lancet. Haematology

**Date:** July 2026

**PMID:** 42392109 | **DOI:** 10.1016/S2352-3026(26)00102-X

**Issuing Body:** European Group for Blood and Bone Marrow Transplantation (EBMT) Practice Harmonization and Guidelines Committee and Lymphoma Working Party

**Disease:** Hodgkin lymphoma (relapsed/refractory, adults)

**Development:** 23 experts; structured literature review + 2-day workshop (Berlin, September 29–30, 2025)

**Key Recommendations:**

- **Salvage therapy before autologous HCT:** Brentuximab vedotin or checkpoint inhibitors (or both); metabolic complete response preferred before transplant.
- **Conditioning for autologous HCT:** BEAM (carmustine, etoposide, cytarabine, melphalan) remains standard.
- **Role of peri-transplantation radiotherapy:** May be considered for PET-positive or residual disease.
- **Brentuximab vedotin consolidation:** Recommended for high-risk patients post-autologous HCT.
- **Allogeneic HCT:** Indicated for eligible patients who relapse after autologous HCT; reduced-intensity conditioning + post-transplantation cyclophosphamide (GVHD prophylaxis) preferred.
- **Maintenance after allogeneic HCT:** Routine maintenance not recommended; relapse management tailored (donor lymphocyte infusion, brentuximab vedotin, checkpoint inhibitors, chemotherapy, radiotherapy, or clinical trial enrollment).

**Prior version comparison:** Not reported (guideline versioning/date of prior edition not stated in the abstract).

**Strength of evidence for recommendations:** Not reported.

### Trials

**Very early PET-guided intensification in advanced-stage classic Hodgkin lymphoma**

| **Key secondary / safety** | Grade 3–4 neutropenia 53/150 (35%); anaemia 18/150 (12%); peripheral sensory neuropathy 9/150 (6%). Serious AEs in 45/150 (30%). No deaths. |
| **Funding** | Takeda Oncology |

**Summary:** PET-guided early intensification with brentuximab vedotin–containing chemotherapy yields high 2-year modified PFS in advanced Hodgkin lymphoma. Most patients with negative PET1 (60%) spared intensive therapy. Single-arm design and lack of OS data limit interpretation of curative intent benefit.

## Belantamab mafodotin + carfilzomib/lenalidomide/dexamethasone in relapsed/refractory multiple myeloma

**Journal** | Blood Advances  
**Date** | 2026-May-12  
**PMID** | 41719502  
**DOI** | 10.1182/bloodadvances.2025019050  
**NCT** | NCT04822337  

**Disease/setting/line** | Relapsed/refractory multiple myeloma (RRMM), ≥1 prior line, lenalidomide-naïve at enrollment

**Phase/design/N** | Phase 1/2, open-label, 3+3 dose escalation; N=19 evaluable

**Population/key eligibility** | RRMM patients, ≥1 prior therapy, no prior progression on full-dose lenalidomide

**Intervention vs comparator** | Belantamab mafodotin 1.4 or 1.9 mg/kg IV every 8 weeks + carfilzomib + lenalidomide + dexamethasone (KRd-b); dose escalation phase only, no concurrent control arm

**Recommended phase 2 dose** | 1.9 mg/kg every 8 weeks; no dose-limiting toxicities at this level

**Primary endpoint** | Not explicitly stated in abstract; ORR reported as efficacy measure

**Primary efficacy results** | 
- Overall response rate: 89.5% (17/19)
- Very good partial response or better: 78.9% (15/19)
- Minimal residual disease negativity: all complete responders (number not reported)

**Overall survival** | 24-month OS rate 85.1%; median OS not reported. Median follow-up 19.3 months.

**Progression-free survival** | 24-month PFS rate 74.3%; median PFS not reported

**Key safety findings** |  
- Keratopathy: 94.7% (18/19), mostly grade 1–2, reversible, no permanent discontinuations required
- Grade ≥3 keratopathy: 31.6% (6/19)
- Hematologic and gastrointestinal toxicities: manageable, consistent with KRd or belantamab monotherapy profiles

**Authors' conclusion** | Deep and durable responses demonstrated; feasible with extended-interval belamaf dosing; further phase 2 evaluation warranted to confirm clinical benefit in RRMM

### IMROZ: Isatuximab-VRd vs VRd in Transplant-Ineligible NDMM

**Journal/Source:** Blood  
**Publication Date:** 2026-06-04  
**PMID:** 41758929  
**DOI:** 10.1182/blood.2025030120  
**NCT:** NCT03319667  

**Disease/Setting/Line:**  
Newly diagnosed multiple myeloma (NDMM), transplant-ineligible, first-line therapy

**Phase/Design/N:**  
Phase III, randomized, multicenter. Total N: not reported in abstract.

**Population/Key Eligibility:**  
Transplant-ineligible patients with newly diagnosed multiple myeloma. Benefit observed in older (>70 years) and frail patient subgroups.

**Intervention vs Comparator:**  
- **Intervention:** Isatuximab + Velcade (bortezomib) + Revlimid (lenalidomide) + dexamethasone (Isa-VRd) induction, followed by Isa-Rd maintenance  
- **Comparator:** Velcade + Revlimid + dexamethasone (VRd) induction, followed by Rd maintenance

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**  
Progression-free survival (PFS) benefit reported in primary analysis; specific point estimates and confidence intervals: **not reported in abstract.** Isa-VRd/Isa-Rd provided "significant" PFS benefit vs VRd/Rd.

**Key Secondary & Landmark Endpoints:**  
- **MRD negativity:** Higher rates of MRD negativity and MRD-negative CR achieved with Isa-VRd/Isa-Rd at end of induction, during maintenance, and up to 60 months of follow-up, compared to VRd/Rd.  
- **Time to progression (TTP):** Significantly prolonged with Isa-VRd/Isa-Rd vs VRd/Rd in patients who converted from MRD negative to MRD positive at any timepoint. TTP also favored Isa-VRd/Isa-Rd in landmark analysis of conversion from MRD-negative (end of induction) to MRD-positive.  
- **Overall survival:** **Not reported.**

**Study Maturity:**  
Follow-up documented to 60 months; primary analysis completed; this publication reports extended landmark analyses of MRD dynamics.

**Refining busulfan exposure enhances pediatric ALL HSCT outcomes: insights from the International FORUM study**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | Blood Advances |
| Publication date | 2026-May-26 |
| PMID | 41779961 |
| DOI | 10.1182/bloodadvances.2025019142 |
| NCT | NCT01949129 |
| Phase | Phase II/III |
| Design | Prospective, international, randomized controlled trial (post-hoc pharmacokinetic analysis of fludarabine-busulfan-thiotepa arm) |
| N enrolled (analysis cohort) | 145 with available busulfan plasma levels |
| Disease / setting / line | Pediatric acute lymphoblastic leukemia (ALL), allogeneic HSCT from HLA-matched donor, conditioning regimen arm |
| Population | Ages 0.5–19.5 years; median follow-up 5.0 years |
| Intervention | Busulfan-containing conditioning (fludarabine-busulfan-thiotepa); therapeutic drug monitoring to achieve target cAUC 73.3–98.0 mg·h/L |
| Comparator | Post-hoc matched cohort receiving total-body irradiation (TBI)-based conditioning (n = 51) |
| Primary endpoints | Event-free survival (EFS); graft-versus-host disease-free relapse-free survival (GRFS) |
| **EFS result** | Optimal busulfan exposure (cAUC 73.3–98.0 mg·h/L): HR 1.93 for nonoptimal exposure (p = 0.008). Underexposure (<73.3 mg·h/L) associated with higher relapse (HR 1.93, p = 0.019). Overexposure (>98.0 mg·h/L) associated with increased treatment-related toxicity and GVHD. |
| **GRFS result** | HR 1.93 for nonoptimal exposure (p = 0.002) |
| **Overall survival** | Reported; no difference between optimal busulfan exposure and matched TBI recipients |
| **Relapse** | Reported; no difference between optimal busulfan exposure and matched TBI recipients |
| Key secondary / exploratory | Optimal busulfan exposure (cAUC 73.3–98.0 mg·h/L) showed no difference in EFS, GRFS, overall survival, or relapse compared to matched TBI recipients (n = 51 each) |

### FELIX Trial: Tumor Burden–Guided Dosing of Obecabtagene Autoleucel in R/R B-ALL

**Journal:** Haematologica | **Date:** 2026-06-01 | **PMID:** 41504229 | **DOI:** 10.3324/haematol.2025.288587 | **NCT:** NCT04404660

**Disease/Setting:** Relapsed/refractory B-cell acute lymphoblastic leukemia (R/R B-ALL), adult patients

**Phase:** Ib/II | **Design:** Open-label, prospective, multicenter | **N enrolled:** not reported (abstract reports stratified efficacy/safety by tumor-burden group)

**Population:** Adults with R/R B-ALL undergoing lymphodepletion; stratified by pre-lymphodepletion bone marrow blast burden (low TB: ≤20%; high TB: >20%)

**Intervention:** Obecabtagene autoleucel (obe-cel), a CD19-targeted autologous CAR-T cell therapy with fast off-rate binding domain, administered as split-dose infusions guided by tumor burden

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary Endpoint & Result:** Not explicitly stated in abstract. Efficacy reported as remission rate (overall remission rate [ORR], presumably complete remission): low-TB group 85%; high-TB group 73%.

**Key Findings:**
- **CAR-T expansion:** tumor burden was a critical driver. A 50-percentage-point increase in BM blasts (70% vs 20%) was associated with 1.9-fold increase in maximal CAR-T expansion (95% CI: 1.4–2.6).
- **Grade ≥3 cytokine release syndrome (CRS):** low-TB 2% vs high-TB 3%.
- **Grade ≥3 immune effector cell-associated neurotoxicity syndrome (ICANS):** low-TB 4% vs high-TB 9%.
- **Overall remission rate:** low-TB 85%, high-TB 73%.

**OS Reported/Reached:** Not reported in abstract.

**Secondary/Other Endpoints:** Pharmacokinetics reported; long-term follow-up, durability, and OS not addressed in provided abstract.


**Title:** Total marrow and lymphoid irradiation in combination with cyclophosphamide and etoposide before haematopoietic cell transplantation for relapsed or refractory acute leukaemia: a single-centre, open-label, phase 2 trial

**Journal:** The Lancet. Haematology  
**Publication date:** June 2026  
**PMID:** 42150590  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S2352-3026(26)00014-1  
**NCT:** NCT02094794

**Disease/Setting:** Relapsed or refractory acute myeloid leukaemia (AML) or acute lymphoblastic leukaemia (ALL); allogeneic haematopoietic cell transplantation (HCT) setting

**Phase:** Phase II  
**Design:** Single-centre, open-label, non-randomized; initial 6-patient safety lead-in followed by phase II cohort  
**N enrolled:** 107 screened; 106 received conditioning and HCT per protocol

**Population/Eligibility:** Ages 16–60 years; relapsed or refractory AML or ALL; recipients of bone marrow or peripheral blood stem cells from sibling, matched, or one allele mismatched unrelated donors

**Intervention:** Total marrow and lymphoid irradiation (TMLI) 2000 cGy (days −9 to −5) + etoposide 60 mg/kg (day −4) + cyclophosphamide 100 mg/kg (day −2), followed by HCT on day 0; graft-versus-host disease prophylaxis with tacrolimus and sirolimus

**Comparator:** None (single-arm trial)

**Primary endpoint:** 2-year progression-free survival (PFS)

**Primary endpoint result:** 2-year PFS estimate 34% (95% CI 25–43%) in all 106 patients

**Overall survival:** Not reported

**Key secondary endpoints/adverse events:**
- Most common grade 3–4 adverse events: cytopenias 96/106 (91%), metabolic disorders 83/106 (78%), oral mucositis 45/106 (42%), diarrhoea 25/106 (24%), nausea 21/106 (20%), palmar-plantar erythrodysesthesia syndrome 11/106 (10%)
- One death from sinusoidal obstruction syndrome attributed to conditioning regimen
- Median follow-up: 1.8 years (IQR 0.6–3.0) for all patients; 3.1 years (2.1–4.9) for patients alive at last contact
- Safety lead-in (6 patients): no unacceptable toxicity reported

**Funding:** National Institutes of Health and Accuray

**Study period:** May 9, 2014 – March 5, 2024; trial closed to accrual

## ITCC-059: Inotuzumab ozogamicin in paediatric very high risk first B-cell ALL relapse

**Journal:** The Lancet. Haematology  
**Date:** 2026-Jul  
**PMID:** 42296977  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S2352-3026(26)00104-3  
**NCT:** not reported

**Disease/setting/line:** Paediatric B-cell acute lymphoblastic leukaemia, very high-risk first relapse, CD22-positive

**Phase/design/N:** Phase II, single-arm, multicentre international; 37 patients enrolled (45 screened), 31 in minimal amended sample size

**Population/eligibility:**
- Age: >1 year and <18 years
- CD22-positive B-cell ALL with very high-risk first relapse (bone marrow or combined relapse <18 months post-initial diagnosis, OR cytogenetic/molecular high-risk features: KMT2A::AFF1, TCF3::PBX1, TCF3::HLF, hypodiploidy, TP53 mutation)
- Karnofsky (age >16) or Lansky (age ≤16) >60%

**Intervention:** Inotuzumab ozogamicin monotherapy (recommended dose per prior phase 1 cohorts); option to combine with chemotherapy

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary endpoint:** Overall response rate (ORR) among first 31 enrolled  
**Result:** 22 of 31 responders; **ORR 71% (80% CI 58–82)**

**Key secondary endpoints / safety (N=37):**
- Grade 3–4 haematologic: neutropenia 35/37 (95%), thrombocytopenia 31/37 (84%)
- Grade 3–4 non-haematologic: febrile neutropenia 11/37 (30%), infections 8/37 (22%, incl. 1 grade 5 lung infection), AST elevation 12/37 (32%), ALT elevation 10/37 (27%)
- Serious adverse events: 17/37 (46%)
- Treatment-related deaths: 0
- Sinusoidal-obstructive syndrome (post-transplant): 4/23 transplanted patients (17%); all resolved with defibrotide
- **Overall survival: not reported**

**Funding:** Pfizer

## Aplastic Anemia

### Trials

**Title:** Novel FABT-Based Conditioning Regimen With Haploidentical Transplantation for Severe Aplastic Anemia: A Prospective, Single-Center, Phase II Clinical Trial

**Journal / Source:** Transplantation and Cellular Therapy

**Date:** May 2026

**PMID:** 41730450 | **DOI:** 10.1016/j.jtct.2025.12.942

**Disease / Setting / Line:** Severe aplastic anemia (SAA); haploidentical hematopoietic stem cell transplantation (Haplo-HSCT) in patients without HLA-identical sibling donors

**Phase / Design / N:** Phase II, prospective single-center study; N = 36 enrolled; no concurrent randomized comparator

**Population / Key Eligibility:** AA patients undergoing Haplo-HSCT (April 2022 to June 2024); median follow-up 21 (range 2–30) months

**Intervention vs Comparator:**
- **Intervention:** FABT regimen (Fludarabine + ATG [low-dose 2 mg/kg/day] + Busulfan + Thiotepa [thiotepa introduced for first time in this protocol]) combined with post-transplant cyclophosphamide (PTCy) for GVHD prevention
- **Comparator:** None (single-arm); narrative comparison to historical "Baltimore regimen"

**Primary Endpoint + Result:** Not explicitly stated. Reported outcomes include:
- **Engraftment:** 100% neutrophil engraftment; 91.7% platelet engraftment; median time to platelet engraftment 13 (8–27) days; median time to neutrophil engraftment 14 (8–21) days
- **Graft Failure:** 0/36 (0%) primary graft failure
- **2-year OS:** 91.7% (33/36 alive at 2 years); 100% in patients <40 years old
- **2-year GVHD-Relapse-Free Survival (GRFS):** 91.7%
- **Acute GVHD:** 27.8% any grade (10/36); 8.3% grade II–IV (3/36)
- **Chronic GVHD:** 11.1% (4/36), all mild cutaneous
- **CMV Reactivation (2-year CIR):** 11.1% (4/36); 0/36 CMV disease

**Key Secondary Outcomes:** Not formally designated. All outcomes above are reported as comparative improvements vs. "traditional Baltimore regimen," but no concurrent control provided.

**OS Reported / Status:** Yes, 2-year OS = 91.7%; follow-up median 21 months (range 2–30). Not stated whether OS is mature or the expected OS trajectory for SAA Haplo-HSCT in this population.

## Sickle Cell Disease

### Guidelines

### Gene Therapy for Sickle Cell Disease: Practice Recommendations from the American Society for Transplantation and Cellular Therapy and the International Society for Cell & Gene Therapy

**Issuing bodies:** American Society for Transplantation and Cellular Therapy (ASTCT); International Society for Cell & Gene Therapy (ISCT)  
**Disease:** Sickle cell disease (SCD)  
**Publication date:** July 2026  
**Journal:** Transplantation and Cellular Therapy  
**PMID:** 41905703  
**DOI:** 10.1016/j.jtct.2026.03.019  

**What changed / scope:**  
Consensus guidance on clinical implementation of ex vivo gene therapies for SCD, reflecting recent regulatory approvals and early clinical experience. Key areas covered:
- Patient eligibility assessment
- Comparative considerations with allogeneic hematopoietic cell transplantation (alloHCT)
- Mobilization and apheresis strategies
- Conditioning with myeloablative chemotherapy
- Fertility preservation
- Psychosocial care
- Manufacturing quality attributes
- Lifelong surveillance for late effects

**Level of evidence / strength:**  
Not reported (derived from early clinical experience and expert consensus).

**Clinical significance:**  
First major consensus guidance harmonizing SCD gene-therapy practice across transplant and cellular-therapy societies; addresses critical implementation gaps including long-term monitoring for late effects.

### Trials

### Base Editing of BCL11A for Sickle Cell Disease (ristoglogene autogetemcel)

**Journal/Source:** The New England Journal of Medicine  
**Date:** 2026-May-07  
**PMID:** 41931046  
**DOI:** 10.1056/NEJMoa2504835  
**NCT:** NCT05456880

**Disease/Setting:** Sickle cell disease; 31 patients aged 12–35 years with ≥4 severe vaso-occlusive crises in the 2 years before enrollment.

**Phase/Design:** Phase 1–2, single-arm, multicenter study. No control arm.

**Intervention:** Autologous CD34+ hematopoietic stem and progenitor cells base-edited to target BCL11A (ristoglogene autogetemcel, risto-cel), dose ≥3.0 × 10⁶ cells/kg, following myeloablative busulfan conditioning (pharmacokinetically guided).

**Comparator:** None (single-arm).

**Primary Endpoint + Result:** Not formally stated in abstract. Reported outcomes include:
- **Engraftment:** Neutrophil at median 17.5 days; platelet at median 19 days.
- **Edited allele fraction:** Mean 67.4% on-target edited alleles in peripheral blood at 6 months.
- **Hemoglobin composition at 6 months:** Mean HbF >60% of total hemoglobin; mean HbS <40% of total hemoglobin (n=13). Maintained throughout follow-up.
- **Vaso-occlusive crises:** No investigator-reported severe vaso-occlusive crises after day 60 post-final transfusion. No formal comparison to pre-treatment rate.

**Secondary Endpoints:** Not separately delineated in abstract.

**Overall Survival:** Not reported.

**N Enrolled/Followed:** 31 patients enrolled and followed; mean follow-up 6.6 months (range 0.3–20.4 months).

**Funding:** Beam Therapeutics (sponsor, product developer).

**Safety:** One treatment-related death (idiopathic pneumonia syndrome). All 31 patients (100%) had ≥1 adverse event; 27 (87%) had grade ≥3 adverse event; 12 (39%) had serious adverse event. Grade 3–4 event rates not itemized in abstract.

**Conclusion per authors:** Treatment with risto-cel was followed by rapid engraftment, durable HbF expression, and reduction in HbS. Supports further investigation.

| Disease / setting / line | Sickle cell disease; children and adolescents (aged 2.9–21.9 years, median 13.5); newly transplanted cohort |
| Phase | Phase II |
| Design | Multicenter, prospective, single-arm clinical trial |
| N enrolled | 38 |
| Population / key eligibility | Children and adolescents with SCD; HLA-identical sibling donors |
| Intervention | Nonmyeloablative HCT conditioning: alemtuzumab, 300 cGy total body irradiation, and sirolimus |
| Comparator | None (single-arm) |
| **Primary endpoint + result** | Event-free survival (EFS) at 2 years: 78.9% (95% CI not reported); overall survival at 2 years: 100% |
| Key secondary endpoints + results | **Secondary graft failure:** 7/38 patients (18.4%) experienced graft failure between day +39 and day +391 with autologous hematologic reconstitution. One additional patient received unconditioned second HCT; 3 additional patients received reduced-intensity second HCT by year 2. **Donor chimerism at 2 years:** median myeloid chimerism 95%; T-cell chimerism 75% (among engrafted patients). **GVHD:** zero cases of acute or chronic GVHD. **Transfusion burden:** median platelet transfusions 0 (IQR 0–3). **Quality of life:** patient-reported health-related quality of life remained stable early post-HCT and significantly improved at 1 year. **OS reported:** yes, 100% at 2 years. |
| Notes | All 38 patients achieved initial engraftment. One patient received unconditioned second HCT; 3 additional patients received reduced-intensity second HCT to avert secondary graft failure by year 2. Authors note regimen modifications are needed to reduce graft failure risk. |


### DREP-HAPLO Phase II Trial – HLA-haploidentical HSCT in Sickle Cell Disease

**Journal/Source:** Haematologica | **Date:** 2026-Jul-01 | **PMID:** 41376570 | **DOI:** 10.3324/haematol.2025.300013

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Severe sickle cell disease (SCD); pediatric and adult patients; curative intent (first/only HSCT reported).

**Phase/Design/N:** Phase II, multicenter, open-label; N = 22 enrolled (median age 17 years, range 12–40).

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Children and adults with severe SCD; eligible for haploidentical HSCT; no explicit major eligibility restrictions reported in abstract.

**Intervention vs Comparator:** 
- **Intervention:** Haploidentical HSCT with reduced-intensity conditioning: 2 Gy total body irradiation, thymoglobulin, cyclophosphamide, fludarabine, thiotepa; T-cell-replete bone marrow infusion; GvHD prophylaxis with post-transplant cyclophosphamide.
- **Comparator:** None (single-arm phase II trial).

**Primary Endpoint & Result:**
- Event-free survival (survival without graft failure and without moderate-to-severe chronic GvHD):
  - 1 year: 68.18% (95% CI: 51.25%–90.70%)
  - 4 years: 61.98% (95% CI: 44.07%–87.19%)

**Key Secondary Endpoints & Results:**
- Overall survival at 4 years: 90.15% (95% CI: 78.03%–100%)
- Rejection-free survival at 4 years: 85.56% (95% CI: 71.63%–100%)
- Moderate-to-severe GvHD: 6 patients (27%); 4 of 6 resolved, leaving 2 patients (9%) with persistent moderate-to-severe GvHD at last follow-up.
- Infectious episodes (grade 2–4) over 24 months: 85 episodes in 21 patients (21/22 = 95% incidence); 38 bacterial; majority resolved (specifics not reported).
- **OS reported and mature at 4 years.**

**Study Quality Notes:**
- Open-label design; primary endpoint (event-free survival) is objective (graft failure, chronic GvHD) but open-label may introduce bias in GvHD grading (investigator-assessed).
- Single-arm phase II; no comparator arm.
- Follow-up: 24 months for infection reporting; 4 years for survival/GvHD outcomes.
- Graft rejection very low (85.56% rejection-free at 4 years), supporting thiotepa incorporation claim.

## Head and Neck Cancer

### Guidelines

**Title:** Reirradiation for recurrent head and neck squamous cell carcinoma: international expert consensus recommendations endorsed by the Reirradiation Collaborative Group, the European Society for Radiotherapy and Oncology Reirradiation Focus Group, and the American Society for Radiation Oncology.

**Journal/Source:** The Lancet Oncology

**Publication Date:** July 2026

**PMID:** 42372755

**DOI:** 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00174-9

**Disease/Setting:** Recurrent or second primary head and neck squamous cell carcinoma (HNSCC) in previously irradiated regions.

**Issuing Body:** International expert consensus (Reirradiation Collaborative Group, European Society for Radiotherapy and Oncology Reirradiation Focus Group, American Society for Radiation Oncology).

**Scope & Key Recommendations:**
Pragmatic guidance across patient selection, imaging, target delineation, treatment planning, dose accumulation, and toxicity management for reirradiation in recurrent/second primary HNSCC. Covers modern conformal radiotherapy techniques including intensity-modulated radiotherapy, proton therapy, and stereotactic body radiotherapy.

**What Changed vs Prior Version:** Not reported (appears to be a new consensus statement).

**Strength/Level of Evidence:** Not reported in abstract (full document review required for detailed evidence grading per recommendation).

**Development Process:** Structured expert consensus process with formal agreement assessment.

### Systemic Treatment of Thyroid Cancer: ASCO Guideline

**Source:** Journal of Clinical Oncology | **Date:** 2026-05-10 | **PMID:** 41921121 | **DOI:** 10.1200/JCO-26-00235

**Issuing body:** American Society of Clinical Oncology (ASCO)

**Disease:** Thyroid cancer (well-differentiated, high-grade/poorly differentiated, anaplastic, medullary)

**Version/date:** 2026; literature search through November 5, 2025

**Evidence base:** 66 publications reviewed (systematic reviews, meta-analyses, RCTs, observational studies from January 2000–November 2025)

**Scope:** Evidence-based recommendations on systemic therapy use across thyroid cancer histologies

**Key recommendation areas:**
- Well-differentiated thyroid cancer
- Differentiated high-grade or poorly differentiated thyroid cancer
- Anaplastic thyroid cancer
- Medullary thyroid cancer

**Outcomes addressed:** Overall survival, disease-free survival, safety

**What changed vs. prior version:** Not reported.

**Link:** https://ascopubs.org/topics/asco-guidelines/head-neck-cancer

### Trials

**RATIONALE-213: Tislelizumab + Chemotherapy/Chemoradiotherapy for Resectable Esophageal Squamous Cell Carcinoma — Final Analysis**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | Clinical Cancer Research |
| Date | 2026-05-15 |
| PMID | 41770095 |
| DOI | 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-2367 |
| Phase | II |
| Design | Multicenter, open-label, two-cohort; nonrandomized |
| Disease | Resectable esophageal squamous cell carcinoma (ESCC) |
| N enrolled | 70 total (30 PET responders, 40 PET nonresponders after induction) |
| Population | Resectable ESCC; stratified by PET/CT response to one cycle of induction chemotherapy (maximum standardized uptake value decrease ≥35% = responder) |
| Intervention | **PET responders:** tislelizumab 200 mg IV × 3 cycles + chemotherapy. **PET nonresponders:** tislelizumab 200 mg IV × 3 cycles + chemoradiotherapy. All followed by surgery. |
| Comparator | None (nonrandomized, single-arm design) |
| **Primary endpoint: pathologic complete response (pCR) rate** | **PET responders:** 30% (95% CI, 11.9–54.3). **PET nonresponders:** 34.4% (95% CI, 18.6–53.2). |
| Key secondary endpoints | • **1-year disease-free survival:** 79% (PET responders), 74.2% (PET nonresponders). • **1-year event-free survival:** 87.1% (PET responders), 67.8% (PET nonresponders). • **Overall survival:** not reported. • Higher baseline PD-L1 tumor area positivity scores associated with higher pCR in both cohorts (exact effect size not reported). |
| Safety (any-grade/grade ≥3 TRAE) | • **PET responders:** 93.3% / 50%. • **PET nonresponders:** 97.5% / 82.5%. Most common grade ≥3 TRAE: decreased neutrophil count (36.7% and 70%, respectively). No new safety signals reported. |
| Median follow-up | 25.5 months (as of 25 October 2024) |

**Appraisal:** Primary endpoint is a surrogate (pCR); OS not reported. Open-label, nonrandomized single-arm design with investigator-assessed pathology. Small cohort sizes yield wide confidence intervals on the primary endpoint. PD-L1 analysis is post-hoc descriptive association, not prespecified hypothesis. High-grade hematologic toxicity in PET nonresponders (70% neutropenia) exceeds PET responders (36.7%), suggesting intensity-dependent tolerability. Follow-up duration modest for long-term survival claims.

**Title:** Covalent FAPI Imaging-Guided Precision Surgery in Patients with Medullary Thyroid Carcinoma: A Phase II Clinical Trial  
**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Date:** 2026-May-01  
**PMID:** 42013308  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-3970  
**NCT:** not reported  

**Disease/setting/line:** Medullary thyroid carcinoma (MTC); newly diagnosed and recurrent disease; surgical resection  

**Phase/design/N:** Phase II, prospective, open-label; N=50 enrolled; stratified into three predefined arms: (i) newly diagnosed MTC with R0 resection (n not reported), (ii) recurrent MTC with R0 resection (n not reported), (iii) unresectable disease or distant metastasis (n not reported)  

**Population/key eligibility:** Patients with medullary thyroid carcinoma; stratification by disease stage and resectability status  

**Intervention vs comparator:** [68Ga]Ga-CTR-FAPI-30 PET-CT-guided surgery vs. conventional imaging (historical comparator)  

**Primary endpoint + result:**  
Biochemical cure rate at 1 month postoperatively:  
- Arm 1 (newly diagnosed, R0): 84.2% (95% CI, 60.4%–96.6%); exceeded historical data (P=0.007–0.049)  
- Arm 2 (recurrent, R0): 46.7% (95% CI, 21.3%–73.4%); exceeded historical data (P=0.007–0.049)  
- Arm 3 (unresectable/metastatic): not reported separately  

**Key secondary endpoints + results:**  
- Diagnostic accuracy of [68Ga]Ga-CTR-FAPI-30 vs. conventional imaging (231 lesions with pathology gold standard): 96.5% vs. 72.7% (P<0.0001)  
- Sensitivity: 98.5% vs. 81.7% (P<0.0001)  
- Specificity: 85.3% vs. 20.6% (P<0.0001)  
- Surgical plan modification rate: 46% of patients; 91% of modifications histopathologically justified  
- Event-free survival: not reported  
- Overall survival: not reported; follow-up duration not reported

Open-label design. No comparator. Adequate for signal-finding but insufficient for practice guidance.

### Head & Neck — Trial

**Title:** First-line zolbetuximab plus mFOLFOX6 and nivolumab in unresectable CLDN18.2-positive gastric or gastroesophageal junction adenocarcinoma: a phase 2 trial.

**Journal/Source:** Nature Medicine

**Date:** June 2026

**PMID:** 41840238 | **DOI:** 10.1038/s41591-026-04306-9 | **NCT:** NCT03505320

**Disease/Setting:** Metastatic gastric/gastroesophageal junction (mG/GEJ) adenocarcinoma, CLDN18.2-positive, HER2-negative; first-line

**Phase:** Phase II

**Design:** Open-label; cohort 4A (safety lead-in) + 4B (expansion phase) of the global ILUSTRO study

**N Enrolled:** 77 patients (85.5% CLDN18.2-high); n=71 in cohort 4B for efficacy analysis

**Population/Eligibility:** Unresectable mG/GEJ adenocarcinoma, CLDN18.2-positive

**Intervention:** Zolbetuximab (CLDN18.2-targeting monoclonal antibody) + mFOLFOX6 (fluorouracil, leucovorin, oxaliplatin) + nivolumab (anti-PD-L1)

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary Endpoint:** Progression-free survival (PFS) per RECIST v1.1, investigator-assessed

**Primary Result:** 
- Cohort 4B median PFS (95% CI): 14.8 months (8.3–not estimable) overall (n=71); 18.0 months (11.1–not estimable) in CLDN18.2-high subgroup (n=59)
- No p-value reported (single-arm)

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**
- Objective response rate (measurable disease, 95% CI): 62.1% (48.4–74.5) in 4B overall (n=58); 68.1% (52.9–80.9) in CLDN18.2-high (n=47)
- Overall survival: not reported

**Safety (Cohorts 4A + 4B combined, n=77):**
- Most common treatment-emergent adverse events: nausea (80.5%), decreased appetite (72.7%)
- Serious adverse events: not reported in abstract

**Clinical Context:** Efficacy and safety findings support randomized evaluation in the ongoing phase 3 LUCERNA study.

## Phase II Trial: Preoperative Chemoimmunotherapy + Salvage Surgery + Adjuvant Tislelizumab in Recurrent HNSCC

**Title:** Preoperative Chemoimmunotherapy Followed by Salvage Surgery and Adjuvant Tislelizumab for Previously Irradiated Recurrent HNSCC: A Prospective Phase II Trial  
**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Publication Date:** 2026-Jul-01  
**PMID:** 41941265  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-4693  
**NCT:** Not reported

---

### Study Design & Population
- **Phase:** II  
- **Design:** Single-arm prospective trial (open-label)  
- **N enrolled:** 34; N surgical: 26  
- **Population:** Resectable recurrent head and neck squamous cell carcinoma (HNSCC) after prior radiotherapy  
- **Key eligibility:** Resectable disease; prior radiotherapy

---

### Intervention
**Preoperative (2 cycles, every 3 weeks):**  
- Tislelizumab 200 mg (anti-PD-1 monoclonal antibody, humanized IgG4)  
- Albumin-bound paclitaxel 260 mg/m²  
- Cisplatin 60–75 mg/m²  

**Surgical:** Salvage surgery (R0 resection achieved in 19/26, 73.1%)  

**Adjuvant:** 6 cycles tislelizumab 200 mg

---

### Primary Endpoint
**Major pathologic response (MPR)** in surgical specimens  
- **Result:** 19.2% (5/26 surgical patients)  
- Pathologic complete response (pCR): 15.4% (4/26)

---

### Key Secondary Endpoints
- **Objective response rate (ORR, preoperative):** 35.3% (12/34 enrolled)  
- **R0 resection:** 73.1% (19/26 surgical)  
- **2-year event-free survival (EFS):** 39.6%  
- **2-year overall survival (OS):** 54.8%  
- **Safety:** Grade 1–2 adverse events common; one grade 3 hyperglycemia; no grade ≥3 immune-related adverse events reported

---

### Biomarker Findings
**Baseline B-cell receptor (BCR) repertoire diversity and clonal abundance:**  
- High baseline clonal abundance (top 1% and top 10%) correlated with poor prognosis  
- Top 1% clonality showed "strong prognostic power" (AUC = 0.910, p = 0.006)  
- Authors propose baseline BCR repertoire as a noninvasive prognostic biomarker

---

### Median Follow-up
32 months

---

### Key Observation
All MPR patients (n=5) remained disease-free at last follow-up.
