| **Safety** | Consistent with interim analysis and known CDK4/6 inhibitor profiles; specific grade 3+ toxicities not reported in abstract |
| **Follow-up** | Median 19 months (IQR 18.5–19.6) at data cutoff |
| **Subgroup analyses** | Consistent PFS benefit across menopausal status, metastatic sites, prior treatment, DFI, ESR1/PIK3CA/TP53 alterations; post-hoc: patients with early-onset diarrhea showed HR 0.49 [95% CI 0.36–0.68] |

**Summary:** Final analysis of BRIGHT-2 confirms PFS benefit with bireociclib + fulvestrant in HR+/HER2− ABC after endocrine progression. Primary endpoint met; OS immature.

**Title:** A Phase II Study of Docetaxel and Pembrolizumab plus Interleukin 12 Gene Therapy in Nonmetastatic, Anthracycline-Refractory Triple-Negative Breast Cancer (INTEGRAL)

**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Publication date:** 2026-May-01  
**PMID:** 41661218  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-2649  
**NCT:** not reported

**Disease/setting/line:** Early-stage triple-negative breast cancer (stages I–III), anthracycline-refractory, neoadjuvant setting

**Phase/design/N:** Phase II, single-arm open-label, N = 8 enrolled (trial terminated early)

**Population/eligibility:** Patients with stages I–III TNBC with residual disease after anthracycline-based neoadjuvant chemotherapy

**Intervention vs comparator:** Neoadjuvant docetaxel 100 mg/m² IV + pembrolizumab 200 mg IV every 3 weeks for 4 cycles; intratumoral ADV/IL12 (adenoviral-mediated interleukin-12) given 3 days prior to cycles 2–4. Initial dose 5 × 10¹¹ viral particles in 2 mL (4 patients); reduced to 3 × 10¹¹ VP (4 patients) due to adverse events. No comparator arm.

**Primary endpoint + result:**  
Pathologic complete response (pCR). **Result:** 1/8 patients (12.5%) achieved pCR; this patient received the lower dose (3 × 10¹¹ VP).

**Key secondary endpoints + results:**  
Safety and toxicity. Grade ≥3 adverse events in 87.5% (7/8 patients); trial terminated early due to toxicity burden. Two treatment-related deaths reported. Immune profiling and CCL4 elevation observed exclusively in the 1 patient with pCR.

**Overall survival:** not reported

**Correlative/translational findings:** Elevation of CCL4 levels associated with pCR achievement in 1 patient.

### TROPION-Breast01: Datopotamab Deruxtecan vs. Chemotherapy in HR+/HER2− Metastatic Breast Cancer — Final OS Analysis

**Title:** Datopotamab deruxtecan versus chemotherapy in previously treated inoperable/metastatic hormone receptor-positive, HER2-negative breast cancer: final overall survival analysis of the phase III TROPION-Breast01 study

**Journal:** Annals of Oncology  
**Publication Date:** May 2026  
**PMID:** 41448362  
**DOI:** 10.1016/j.annonc.2025.12.017  
**NCT:** NCT05104866

**Disease/Setting:** Previously treated inoperable/metastatic HR-positive, HER2-negative breast cancer; patients with progression on endocrine therapy and 1–2 prior lines of chemotherapy in the metastatic setting.

**Phase & Design:** Phase III, randomized controlled trial, 1:1 allocation, multicentre, blinded independent central review (BICR) for PFS assessment.

**Population:** Patients with inoperable/metastatic HR+/HER2− breast cancer, disease progression on endocrine therapy, endocrine therapy unsuitable, 1–2 prior lines of metastatic chemotherapy. N enrolled: not reported in abstract.

**Intervention vs. Comparator:**
- **Intervention:** Datopotamab deruxtecan (Dato-DXd) 6 mg/kg IV every 3 weeks
- **Comparator:** Investigator's choice of chemotherapy (ICC): eribulin, capecitabine, vinorelbine, or gemcitabine

**Primary Endpoints & Results:**
1. **Progression-free survival (PFS) by BICR:** met (data from prior analysis referenced; final OS analysis does not restate PFS numbers)
2. **Overall survival (OS):** **did not reach statistical significance**
   - Hazard ratio: 1.01
   - 95% CI: 0.83–1.22
   - p-value: 0.9445
   - Median follow-up: 22.8 months

**Key Secondary Endpoints (continued to favor Dato-DXd):**
- PFS by investigator assessment: favored Dato-DXd
- Objective response rate: favored Dato-DXd
- Duration of response: favored Dato-DXd
- Disease control rate at 12 weeks: favored Dato-DXd
- Time to first and second subsequent therapy or death: favored Dato-DXd
- Time to second progression or death: favored Dato-DXd
- Specific numeric values for secondary endpoints: not reported in abstract

**Safety:** Overall safety profile of Dato-DXd remained favorable compared with ICC; no new safety signals with longer follow-up.

**Key Imbalance:** Subsequent ADC use (trastuzumab deruxtecan, sacituzumab govitecan) was imbalanced: 12.3% (Dato-DXd) vs. 24.0% (ICC). Authors note this imbalance may have affected OS results.

**Authors' Conclusion:** Study met primary endpoint of PFS by BICR. While OS improvement was not statistically significant, subsequent ADC treatment imbalance may have confounded OS. Totality of efficacy and safety data supports Dato-DXd as a treatment option for previously treated, inoperable/metastatic HR+/HER2− breast cancer.

### PLANeT Trial (Pembrolizumab Low dose in Addition to NACT in TNBC)

**Journal** | Annals of Oncology  
**Date** | May 2026  
**PMID** | 41443410  
**DOI** | 10.1016/j.annonc.2025.12.015

**Disease / setting / line** | Triple-negative breast cancer (TNBC), stage II–III, neoadjuvant setting, non-metastatic

**Phase / design / N** | Phase II, open-label randomized controlled trial; N = 157 enrolled, 152 underwent surgery

**Population / key eligibility**
- Previously untreated stage II–III TNBC
- Enrolled at a tertiary cancer center in New Delhi, India
- Lacked access to standard-dose pembrolizumab (stated as eligibility criterion)

**Intervention vs. comparator**
- **Intervention:** Dose-dense NACT (4 cycles doxorubicin–cyclophosphamide, then 4 cycles paclitaxel) + low-dose pembrolizumab (50 mg IV every 6 weeks for 3 cycles; total ~9 months)
- **Comparator:** NACT alone

**Primary endpoint + result**
- **Pathological complete response (pCR)**
  - Low-dose pembrolizumab + NACT: 53.8% (90% CI 43.9%–63.5%, intention-to-treat)  
  - NACT alone: 40.5% (90% CI 31.1%–50.4%)  
  - Absolute difference: 13.3% (90% CI 0.3%–26.3%); one-sided p = 0.047
  - Among surgical cohort (N = 152): 56.7% vs. 41.0% (absolute difference 15.7%, one-sided p = 0.031)

**Key secondary / safety**
- Grade ≥3 toxicity: 50% (low-dose pembrolizumab) vs. 59.5% (control)
- **Overall survival: not reported**
- Event-free or recurrence-free survival: not reported

**Notes**
- Enrollment period: February 2024 – February 2025
- One-sided hypothesis testing used; confidence interval for primary endpoint boundary crosses zero
- Authors state benefit "appears numerically similar to KEYNOTE-522" (historical comparison, not prespecified)
- Explicitly positioned as cost-effective alternative for settings with restricted access, not as an efficacy-equivalent or superior strategy

## CAPItello-290: Capivasertib + paclitaxel for mTNBC (phase III, global)

**Journal** | Annals of Oncology  
**Date** | May 2026  
**PMID** | 41422862  
**DOI** | 10.1016/j.annonc.2025.12.012  

**Disease / setting / line** | Triple-negative breast cancer (mTNBC), first-line metastatic  
**Phase** | III  
**Design** | Randomized (1:1), double-blind (placebo-controlled), global, multicenter  
**N enrolled** | 812 total; 30.7% with PIK3CA/AKT1/PTEN-altered tumours  

**Population** | Previously untreated metastatic TNBC  

**Intervention vs comparator**  
- Arm A: Capivasertib (pan-AKT inhibitor) + paclitaxel 80 mg/m²  
- Arm B: Placebo + paclitaxel 80 mg/m²  

**Primary endpoint: Overall survival (OS)**  

*Overall population (data cutoff 18 March 2024):*  
- Median OS capivasertib-paclitaxel: 17.7 months  
- Median OS placebo-paclitaxel: 18.0 months  
- HR 0.92 (95% CI 0.78–1.08), P = 0.3239  
- **Primary endpoint NOT MET**  

*PIK3CA/AKT1/PTEN-altered subgroup:*  
- Median OS capivasertib-paclitaxel: 20.4 months  
- Median OS placebo-paclitaxel: 20.4 months  
- HR 1.05 (95% CI 0.77–1.43), P = 0.7602  
- **No benefit**  

**Key secondary: Progression-free survival (PFS)**  

*Overall population (data cutoff 25 May 2022):*  
- Median PFS capivasertib-paclitaxel: 5.6 months  
- Median PFS placebo-paclitaxel: 5.1 months  
- HR 0.72 (95% CI 0.61–0.84)  
- Numerically favoured capivasertib; OS was not reported at this PFS cutoff  

*PIK3CA/AKT1/PTEN-altered subgroup:*  
- Median PFS capivasertib-paclitaxel: 7.5 months  
- Median PFS placebo-paclitaxel: 5.6 months  
- HR 0.70 (95% CI 0.52–0.95)  

**Safety (grade ≥3 adverse events)**  
- Most frequent: diarrhoea — 12.7% (capivasertib-paclitaxel) vs 0.7% (placebo-paclitaxel)  
- Discontinuation due to AE: 8.5% (capivasertib-paclitaxel) vs 4.9% (placebo-paclitaxel)  
- Deaths attributed to AE: 4.2% (all patients)  

**Conclusions** (per abstract)  
Capivasertib-paclitaxel did not meet the prespecified boundary for OS improvement in the overall population or the PIK3CA/AKT1/PTEN-altered subgroup. PFS numerically favoured the combination, especially in the altered-tumour subgroup. Safety was manageable and consistent with prior data.

**Title:** Computationally Derived Spatial Immune Signature Identifies Trastuzumab Responders in HER2+ Breast Cancer: NSABP B-41 Clinical Trial Validation.  
**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Date:** 2026-06-15  
**PMID:** 41915435  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-4185  
**NCT:** Not reported

**Disease/setting/line of therapy:** HER2-positive breast cancer; adjuvant setting

**Phase:** III  
**Design:** Post-hoc analysis of randomized controlled trial; NSABP B-41 compared chemotherapy + trastuzumab vs. chemotherapy + lapatinib vs. chemotherapy + combination. N = 221 evaluable (61 DeSTIL-positive, 160 DeSTIL-negative).  
**Population:** HER2+ breast cancer patients from NSABP B-41 trial with available H&E slides for computational analysis

**Intervention:** Computationally derived spatial immune signature (DeSTIL) scoring from hematoxylin and eosin slides, stratifying patients into positive or negative groups; association tested with trastuzumab vs. combination treatment response

**Primary endpoint + result:**  
Event-free survival (EFS) by treatment arm and DeSTIL status:  
- DeSTIL-positive patients (n=61): trastuzumab arm vs. combination arm: HR = 0.09 (95% CI 0.01–0.77); P = 0.006  
- Signature-treatment interaction: P = 0.024  
- DeSTIL-negative patients (n=160): no EFS difference observed  

**Key secondary/exploratory endpoints:**  
Pathologic complete response classifier (trained on University Hospitals Cleveland slides): AUC = 0.70 in training cohort; AUC = 0.63 in trastuzumab arm of NSABP B-41 validation cohort

**Overall survival:** Not reported

**neoCARHP Trial — Neoadjuvant Taxane ± Carboplatin in HER2-Positive Breast Cancer**

- **Journal / Source:** Journal of Clinical Oncology
- **Publication Date:** 2026-Jun-10
- **PMID:** 41576297
- **DOI:** 10.1200/JCO-25-02176
- **NCT:** not reported

**Disease / Setting / Line of Therapy:**
Stage II–III HER2-positive invasive breast cancer; neoadjuvant setting; previously untreated

**Phase / Design / N:**
- Phase III, multicenter, randomized, noninferiority trial
- N = 766 in modified intention-to-treat population (382 THP, 384 TCbHP)
- Enrolled April 30, 2021–August 27, 2024

**Population / Key Eligibility:**
Women age ≥18 years with previously untreated stage II–III HER2-positive invasive breast cancer

**Intervention vs. Comparator:**
- **THP:** Investigator-selected taxane (docetaxel, paclitaxel, or nab-paclitaxel) + trastuzumab + pertuzumab; 6 cycles, 3-week intervals
- **TCbHP:** Same as THP + carboplatin

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**
- **Endpoint:** Pathologic complete response (pCR, ypT0/is ypN0) in breast and axilla
- **THP:** 245/382 (64.1%, 95% CI 59.1–69.0%)
- **TCbHP:** 253/384 (65.9%, 95% CI 60.9–70.6%)
- **Absolute difference:** −1.8% (95% CI −8.5 to 5.0%)
- **Odds ratio:** 0.93 (95% CI 0.69–1.25)
- **p-value / significance:** not reported
- **Noninferiority conclusion:** THP met noninferiority to TCbHP

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**
Safety outcomes (improved tolerability with THP); OS not reported

**Clinical Bottom Line (authors):**
Omitting carboplatin may be applicable in HER2-positive breast cancer given noninferior pCR and improved tolerability.

### FAST-Forward: 10-year efficacy and late normal tissue effects

**Journal/source:** The Lancet Oncology  
**Publication date:** June 2026  
**PMID:** 42134381  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00076-8  
**Trial identifier:** ISRCTN19906132  

**Disease/setting/line:** Early-stage invasive breast cancer (pT1–3, pN0–1, M0) after breast conservation surgery or mastectomy; adjuvant radiotherapy  

**Phase/design:** Phase III, multicentre, open-label, non-inferiority, randomized controlled trial (equivalence trial); 97 hospitals (47 radiotherapy centres, 50 referring hospitals) in the UK. Allocation not masked due to nature of intervention.  

**N enrolled:** Main trial: 4110 participants enrolled, 4087 included in intention-to-treat population (23 withdrew consent for data use). Randomization: 40 Gy (n=1358), 27 Gy (n=1362), 26 Gy (n=1367). Nodal substudy: 469 enrolled, 466 included in intention-to-treat analyses.  

**Population/key eligibility:** Patients ≥18 years with invasive carcinoma of breast (pT1–3, pN0–1, M0) after breast conservation surgery or mastectomy.  

**Intervention vs comparator:**  
- **40 Gy in 15 fractions over 3 weeks** (standard, comparator)  
- **27 Gy in 5 fractions over 1 week** (test arm)  
- **26 Gy in 5 fractions over 1 week** (test arm)  

All to whole breast or chest wall. Nodal substudy assessed same schedules in patients requiring axillary treatment.  

**Primary endpoint and result:**  
Non-inferiority of ipsilateral breast recurrence at 5 years (reported as 10-year cumulative incidence):  
- **40 Gy:** 10-year cumulative incidence 3.6% (95% CI 2.7–4.9); 45 events/1358 participants  
- **27 Gy:** 10-year cumulative incidence 2.9% (95% CI 2.1–4.0); 41 events/1362 participants  
- **26 Gy:** 10-year cumulative incidence 2.1% (95% CI 1.5–3.1); 30 events/1367 participants  

Non-inferiority criterion met for both 27 Gy and 26 Gy vs 40 Gy. *p-value not reported in abstract.*  

**Key secondary endpoints:**  
- **10-year clinician-reported moderate or marked breast or chest wall effects:**  
  - 40 Gy: 100/765 (13.1%)  
  - 27 Gy: 157/814 (19.3%)  
  - 26 Gy: 111/770 (14.4%)  
- **Nodal substudy (5-year follow-up):** 32 locoregional recurrences reported; efficacy described as "reassuring" but sample size limits precision.  
- **Overall survival:** Not reported as a separate endpoint; not discussed as primary or key secondary outcome.  

**Follow-up:** Main trial median 10.1 years (IQR 10.0–10.2); nodal substudy median 7.0 years (IQR 6.2–7.1).  

**Interpretation (per authors):** Long-term follow-up confirms 26 Gy in 5 fractions over 1 week is safe and efficacious for adjuvant radiotherapy to breast or chest wall, supporting its use as standard of care. Efficacy for this schedule in axillary nodal setting is reassuring but substudy sample size limits precision.  

**Funding:** UK National Institute for Health and Care Research.

| **Median follow-up** | 22.2 years (IQR 20.1–24.5) |
| **Key eligibility** | Women ≤75 years; unilateral histologically confirmed stage I–III breast adenocarcinoma; pathologically node-negative (pN0); central or medial primary location |
| **Funding** | Ligue Nationale contre le Cancer, KWF Kankerbestrijding, EORTC Cancer Research Fund |
| **Study status** | Closed after final analysis |

**Interpretation:** Breast cancer mortality was significantly reduced with IM-MS irradiation, but this was offset by a numerically higher non-breast cancer mortality after 15 years, resulting in **no long-term OS benefit**. Long-term organ toxicity (cardiac and pulmonary fibrosis) documented. Authors emphasize need for advanced radiation techniques to reduce off-target dose.

**SUBITO: Intensified chemotherapy vs olaparib in stage III HER2-negative HRD breast cancer**

- **Journal / Source:** The Lancet Oncology
- **Publication Date:** July 2026
- **PMID:** 42372741
- **DOI:** 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00131-2
- **NCT:** not reported

**Disease / Setting / Line of Therapy**  
Stage IIIA–C, HER2-negative, homologous recombination deficient (HRD) breast cancer; newly diagnosed; adjuvant setting (no prior chemotherapy stated).

**Phase / Design / N Enrolled**  
Phase III, open-label, randomized controlled trial. N = 174 enrolled (IACT n = 87; olaparib n = 87). Median follow-up 41 months (IQR 27–59).

**Population / Key Eligibility**  
Female, age 18–66 years, stage IIIA–C HER2-negative breast cancer without distant metastases. HRD defined by pathogenic germline BRCA1/2 mutation or evidence of HRD tumor on testing. 28 (32%) in IACT group and 22 (25%) in olaparib group had germline BRCA1/2 mutations. Median age 42 years (IQR 37–50). All female.

**Intervention vs Comparator**  
- **IACT arm (n = 87):** Dose-dense alkylating chemotherapy (ddAC; doxorubicin 60 mg/m² plus further details not fully reported in abstract) followed by autologous stem cell rescue.
- **Olaparib arm (n = 87):** Conventional chemotherapy followed by olaparib (maintenance regimen details not reported).

**Primary Endpoint + Result**  
4-year overall survival:  
- IACT: 77.0% (95% CI 67.7–87.7)  
- Olaparib: 76.4% (95% CI 66.9–87.4)  
- Hazard ratio for death: 1.11 (95% CI 0.57–2.17)  
- p = 0.37  
**Interpretation:** No significant difference; CI overlaps 1.0. Study met its primary objective of assessing non-inferiority / equivalence.

**Key Secondary Endpoints**  
Adverse events (Grade 3–4):  
- Platelet count decreased: IACT 80/81 (99%) vs olaparib 18/91 (19%)  
- Neutrophil count decreased: IACT 77/81 (95%) vs olaparib 56/91 (61%)  
- Anemia: IACT 50/81 (62%) vs olaparib 37/91 (41%)  
- Treatment-emergent serious adverse events: IACT 38/81 (47%) vs olaparib 24/91 (26%)  
- Febrile neutropenia (most common SAE): IACT 36/81 (44%) vs olaparib 11/91 (12%)  
- Treatment-related deaths: 0 in both arms.

**Overall survival reported and mature:** Yes; 4-year OS data at median 41-month follow-up.


## Concurrent Versus Sequential Radiation Dose Escalation to the Surgical Cavity for Conservative Treatment of High-Risk Early Breast Cancer: NRG/RTOG 1005 Phase III Trial

**Journal:** Journal of Clinical Oncology  
**Publication Date:** July 2026  
**PMID:** 42114027  
**DOI:** 10.1200/JCO-25-02465  
**NCT:** not reported  

**Disease/Setting:** Early breast cancer, high-risk for ipsilateral breast recurrence (IBR) after lumpectomy and axillary surgery; breast conservation therapy.  

**Phase/Design:** Phase III, randomized controlled trial, multicenter (NRG/RTOG 1005).  
**N Enrolled:** 2,354 patients randomly assigned; 2,255 eligible for analysis (sequential arm n = 1,118; concurrent arm n = 1,137).  

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Patients with breast cancer undergoing breast conservation, deemed at higher risk for ipsilateral breast recurrence after lumpectomy and axillary surgery.  

**Intervention vs. Comparator:**  
- **Sequential arm:** 12 Gy boost in 6 fractions or 14 Gy in 7 fractions *after* whole-breast irradiation (WBI) of 50 Gy in 25 fractions or 42.7 Gy in 16 fractions.  
- **Concurrent arm:** 8 Gy boost in 15 fractions (0.53 Gy per day) *during* WBI of 40 Gy in 15 fractions.  
- Modality: 3D conformal RT or intensity-modulated RT permitted in both arms.  

**Primary Endpoint & Result:**  
Ipsilateral breast recurrence (IBR) as first recurrence, noninferiority design.  
Noninferiority criterion **met:**  
- 5-year IBR: sequential 2.1%, concurrent 1.9%  
- 7-year IBR: sequential 2.2%, concurrent 2.6%  
- HR (90% CI): 1.31 (0.84 to 2.04); noninferiority margin HR upper limit 2.12 on 90% CI  
- Total IBR events: 56 over median follow-up of 7.3 years  

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**  
- Disease-free survival: not reported  
- Overall survival: not reported (immature at median follow-up 7.3 years)  
- Adverse events: stated as no worsening in concurrent arm; details not reported in abstract  
- Cosmetic outcomes: stated as no worsening in concurrent arm; details not reported in abstract  

**Conclusion per Abstract:**  
Concurrent boost during WBI is noninferior to sequential boost for IBR without worsening toxicity or cosmetic outcomes, and reduces overall treatment time.

### OPTIMAL — Phase III Trial: Oral Paclitaxel vs IV Paclitaxel in HER2-Negative Metastatic Breast Cancer

**Title:** OPTIMAL: a multinational phase III study of oral paclitaxel (DHP107) versus intravenous weekly paclitaxel in HER2-negative recurrent or metastatic breast cancer.

**Journal/Source:** Annals of Oncology (official journal of the European Society for Medical Oncology)  
**Publication Date:** July 2026  
**PMID:** 41833903  
**DOI:** 10.1016/j.annonc.2026.03.002  
**NCT:** not reported

---

**Disease / Setting / Line of Therapy:** HER2-negative recurrent or metastatic breast cancer; first-line chemotherapy in the metastatic setting.

**Phase:** III  
**Design:** Multinational, multicenter, open-label, randomized, noninferiority trial. Predefined noninferiority margin: HR 1.33.

**N Enrolled:** 549 patients randomly assigned (DHP107 n=277; paclitaxel n=272); 519 included in per-protocol set (PPS).

**Population / Key Eligibility:** Patients with recurrent or metastatic breast cancer; no prior chemotherapy in the metastatic setting. HER2-negative status required.

**Intervention vs Comparator:** 
- DHP107 (oral formulation of paclitaxel, 200 mg/m² [dose incomplete in abstract])
- vs IV paclitaxel (weekly schedule, standard formulation)

---

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**  
Noninferiority of PFS (DHP107 vs paclitaxel):  
- Median PFS: 10.0 months (DHP107) vs 8.5 months (paclitaxel)  
- HR 0.869; 95% CI 0.707–1.068  
- **Noninferiority demonstrated** (CI does not cross 1.33).

**Key Secondary Endpoints + Results:**  
- **Overall survival (OS):** Median OS 32.6 months (DHP107) vs 31.8 months (paclitaxel); HR 0.967, 95% CI 0.762–1.227. **OS not significantly different; CI crosses 1.0.**
- **Adverse events:** 
  - Higher in DHP107 group: neutropenia, febrile neutropenia, nausea, diarrhea, vomiting
  - Higher in paclitaxel group: peripheral neuropathy, hypersensitivity reactions
  - Treatment-related mortality: 0/277 (DHP107) vs 1/272 (0.4%, paclitaxel)
- **Quality of life:** Comparable between groups.

---

**Appraisal Flags:**  
- Open-label design with potential for bias in subjective safety/tolerability reporting
- OS confidence interval crosses 1.0, indicating OS equivalence not definitively demonstrated

### HARMONi-6: Ivonescimab + chemotherapy vs tislelizumab + chemotherapy in advanced squamous NSCLC

**Journal/Source:** The Lancet  
**Publication Date:** 2026-06-27  
**PMID:** 42218899  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S0140-6736(26)00966-9  
**NCT:** NCT05840016  

**Disease/Setting:** Advanced squamous non-small-cell lung cancer (unresectable stage IIIB, IIIC, or IV), first-line, treatment-naïve

**Phase/Design:** Phase III, double-blind, randomized controlled trial, multicenter (50 hospitals in China)

**N Enrolled:** 532 patients randomized (266 per arm); 494 male (93%), 38 female (7%); median age 64 years (IQR 59–69)

**Population/Eligibility:** Age 18–75, pathologically confirmed squamous NSCLC, ECOG PS 0–1, no prior treatment for advanced disease

**Intervention vs Comparator:**
- **Intervention:** Ivonescimab + paclitaxel + carboplatin (4 cycles induction), then ivonescimab maintenance
- **Comparator:** Tislelizumab + paclitaxel + carboplatin (4 cycles induction), then tislelizumab maintenance

**Primary Endpoint:** Progression-free survival (independent radiographic review, RECIST 1.1)  
*Result from prior report:* ivonescimab significantly prolonged PFS vs tislelizumab (not repeated in this abstract)

**Key Secondary Endpoint — Overall Survival (interim analysis):**
- **Data cutoff:** 2026-02-27
- **Events:** 204 deaths (84 in ivonescimab arm [32%]; 120 in tislelizumab arm [45%])
- **Median follow-up:** 21.4 months (95% CI 20.7–21.9)
- **Median OS — Ivonescimab:** 27.9 months (95% CI 27.8–NE)
- **Median OS — Tislelizumab:** 23.7 months (95% CI 20.1–NE)
- **Hazard ratio for death:** 0.66 (95% CI 0.50–0.87)
- **p-value:** not reported in abstract (stated "p" but value truncated)
- **Interpretation (per authors):** Statistically significant and clinically meaningful OS improvement with ivonescimab + chemotherapy

**Safety:** Analyzed in 532 patients who received at least one dose. Adverse events related to treatment, immunity, and VEGF blockade tracked. Details not reported in abstract.

**Study Status:** Enrollment complete; ongoing for treatment and follow-up.

**Funding:** Akeso Biopharma

## OptiTROP-Lung05: Sacituzumab Tirumotecan + Pembrolizumab vs Pembrolizumab Alone in PD-L1+ Advanced NSCLC (Interim)

**Journal:** The Lancet  
**Publication Date:** 2026-Jun-27  
**PMID:** 42214392  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S0140-6736(26)00968-2  
**NCT:** NCT06448312  

**Disease/Setting:** Locally advanced or metastatic NSCLC without targetable genomic alterations; PD-L1 TPS ≥1%; first-line therapy  

**Phase:** III  

**Design:** Randomized, open-label, multicenter (68 hospitals in China); blinded independent central review for PFS  

**N Enrolled:** 413 randomized (sac-TMT + pembrolizumab: n=208; pembrolizumab alone: n=205)  

**Population:** Patients with locally advanced or metastatic NSCLC, PD-L1 TPS ≥1%, no targetable genomic alterations. Screening: 741; randomized: 413.  

**Intervention:** Sacituzumab tirumotecan 4 mg/kg on days 1, 15, 29 + pembrolizumab 400 mg fixed dose day 1, repeated every 6 weeks  

**Comparator:** Pembrolizumab alone, repeated every 6 weeks  

**Primary Endpoint:** Progression-free survival (PFS) by blinded independent central review, intention-to-treat population  

**Primary Result:**  
- Median PFS (sac-TMT + pembrolizumab): not reached  
- Median PFS (pembrolizumab alone): 5.7 months  
- Stratified HR: 0.35 (95% CI 0.26–0.47; p<0.0001)  

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**  
- PFS by PD-L1 TPS subgroup:  
  - PD-L1 TPS 1–49%: HR 0.28 (95% CI 0.19–0.41)  
  - PD-L1 TPS ≥50%: HR 0.47 (95% CI 0.29–0.77)  
- Overall survival: not reported (trial ongoing; final analysis to be reported later)  

**Safety:**  
- Grade 3+ treatment-emergent adverse events:  
  - sac-TMT + pembrolizumab: 115/208 (55%)  
  - pembrolizumab: 64/204 (31%)  

**Median Follow-up:** 10.5 months (IQR 8.7–12.5)  

**Status:** Interim analysis; recruitment complete; trial ongoing.  

**Funding:** Sichuan Kelun-Biotech Biopharmaceutical

### RECLAIM: Radiotherapy + Anti-CTLA-4/PD-1 after anti-PD-1 failure in metastatic NSCLC

**Journal:** Journal for Immunotherapy of Cancer  
**Publication date:** 2026-Jun-22  
**PMID:** 42331381  
**DOI:** 10.1136/jitc-2025-014724  
**NCT:** 2020-001097-29  

**Disease/setting:** Metastatic NSCLC with low (1–49%) or negative (<1%) PD-L1 expression; progressed after first-line anti-PD-1 therapy.  

**Phase | Design | N:** Phase II | single-arm, prospective | 31 enrolled (intention-to-treat).  

**Eligibility (key):** Metastatic NSCLC; PD-L1 <1% or 1–49%; disease progression after first-line anti-PD-1.  

**Intervention:** Ipilimumab (IPI) 1 mg/kg IV every 6 weeks + nivolumab (NIVO) 240 mg IV every 2 weeks for 6 weeks, combined with subablative radiotherapy (3×8 Gy to 1–4 lesions). Maintenance: IPI 1 mg/kg Q6W + NIVO 360 mg Q3W.  

**Comparator:** None (single-arm).  

**Primary endpoints + results:**
- Objective response rate (ORR) at 6 weeks: 7%; at 12 weeks: 10%; best response: 29%.
- Disease control rate (DCR) at 6 weeks: 58%; at 12 weeks: 39%.
- Safety: all 31 patients experienced treatment-related AEs; grade ≥3 in 8 patients (26%); immune-related AEs led to discontinuation in 5 (16%).

**Overall survival (reported but not primary endpoint):**
- Median OS differed significantly by best response: 3.1 months (progressive disease), 13.5 months (stable disease), 22.5 months (partial/complete response); p < 0.001.
- Follow-up duration: not reported.

**Key secondary findings:**
- Baseline sum of longest diameters, age, blood inflammatory markers, and albumin levels were identified as prognostic of treatment response (post-hoc analysis).
- Early T-cell activation in peripheral blood (day 8) was detectable and more pronounced in responders vs progressors.

**Conclusion per authors:** IPI/NIVO/RT induced objective responses in a subset of patients with low/negative PD-L1 who had progressed on first-line anti-PD-1; associated with strong T-cell activation, improved OS, and acceptable safety.

## Trial: Neoadjuvant camrelizumab + chemotherapy in resectable stage IIIA-IIIB NSCLC — biomarker substudy

**Title:** Neoadjuvant camrelizumab plus chemotherapy in resectable stage IIIA-IIIB non-small cell lung cancer: integrated multidimensional biomarker analysis from a phase II study.

**Journal:** Journal for Immunotherapy of Cancer  
**Publication date:** 2026-06-19  
**PMID:** 42320986  
**DOI:** 10.1136/jitc-2026-015604  
**NCT:** NCT06241807

**Disease/setting:** Resectable NSCLC, stage IIIA-IIIB; neoadjuvant intent (preoperative).

**Phase | Design | N:**  
Phase II, single-arm (no comparator). N = 30 enrolled; 27 underwent radical resection.

**Population:**  
Resectable stage IIIA-IIIB NSCLC. Histology: 22 squamous, 8 adenocarcinoma.

**Intervention:**  
Camrelizumab (PD-1 inhibitor) plus chemotherapy × 3 cycles, followed by surgical resection.

**Comparator:**  
None (single-arm).

**Primary endpoint + result:**  
Pathological complete response (pCR). **Result:** 33.3% (9/27 resected patients).

**Key secondary endpoints:**  
- Major pathological response (MPR): 50.0% (13/27 resected).  
- Disease-free survival (DFS) at 2 years: 77.4% (median follow-up 27.2 months).  
- Grade ≥3 treatment-related adverse events: 13.3%.

**OS:** Not reported.

**Exploratory/biomarker findings:**  
- Baseline CD8+ T cells and naive-like T cells (blood and tumor microenvironment) associated with pCR achievement.  
- Elevated baseline CD8+ naive-like T cells and their proximity to tumor cells correlated with improved DFS.  
- Higher baseline circulating CCL3 (chemokine (C-C motif) ligand 3) associated with pCR and prolonged DFS.  
- Post-treatment ctDNA positivity predicted shorter DFS; ctDNA monitoring detected relapse up to 17.6 months before radiographic progression.

**Conclusions per authors:**  
Baseline CD8+ naive-like T-cell abundance, CCL3 levels, and ctDNA dynamics may serve as prognostic biomarkers in this population.

### SKYSCRAPER-06: Tiragolumab + Atezolizumab + Chemotherapy vs Pembrolizumab + Chemotherapy in Advanced Nonsquamous NSCLC

**Journal** | JAMA Oncology  
**Date** | 2026-06-01  
**PMID** | 42060297  
**DOI** | 10.1001/jamaoncol.2026.0818  
**NCT** | NCT04619797  

**Disease / Setting / Line**  
Advanced (locally advanced unresectable or metastatic) nonsquamous non-small cell lung cancer; previously untreated (first-line)  

**Phase | Design | N**  
Phase 3 | Randomized, placebo-controlled, multicenter (129 sites, 21 countries) | 542 enrolled (269 tiragolumab + atezolizumab + chemotherapy; 273 placebo + pembrolizumab + chemotherapy)  

**Population / Key Eligibility**  
Previously untreated patients with locally advanced unresectable or metastatic nonsquamous NSCLC. Mean age 63.6 years (SD 9.3); 65.1% male. Baseline demographics similar between arms.  

**Intervention vs Comparator**  
- **Intervention:** Tiragolumab 600 mg + atezolizumab 1200 mg + chemotherapy (pemetrexed 500 mg/m² + carboplatin AUC 5 or cisplatin 75 mg/m²) IV on day 1 of each 21-day cycle until progression, loss of benefit, unacceptable toxicity, or withdrawal  
- **Comparator:** Placebo + pembrolizumab 200 mg + chemotherapy (same regimen) IV on day 1 of each 21-day cycle until progression, loss of benefit, unacceptable toxicity, or withdrawal  

**Primary Endpoints + Results**  
1. **Investigator-assessed progression-free survival:**  
   - Tiragolumab + atezolizumab + chemotherapy: median 8.3 months (95% CI 7.1–9.6)  
   - Placebo + pembrolizumab + chemotherapy: median 9.9 months (95% CI 8.7–11.9)  
   - Hazard ratio 1.27 (95% CI 1.02–1.57); P = 0.99 (did not meet primary endpoint; favored comparator)  

2. **Overall survival:**  
   - Tiragolumab + atezolizumab + chemotherapy: median 18.9 months (95% CI 15.2–23.8)  
   - Placebo + pembrolizumab + chemotherapy: median 23.1 months (95% CI 20.7–33.0)  
   - Hazard ratio 1.33 (95% CI 1.02–1.73); P = 0.98 (did not meet primary endpoint; favored comparator)  

**Key Secondary Endpoints | Safety**  
Not specified in abstract.  

**Safety (Grade 3–4 Adverse Events)**  
- Tiragolumab + atezolizumab + chemotherapy: 164/267 (61.4%)  
- Placebo + pembrolizumab + chemotherapy: 165/272 (60.7%)  
- **Grade 5 adverse events:**  
  - Tiragolumab + atezolizumab + chemotherapy: 27/267 (10.1%)  
  - Placebo + pembrolizumab + chemotherapy: 16/272 (5.9%)  

**Conclusion**  
Primary endpoints not met. Trial terminated. Experimental arm (tiragolumab + atezolizumab + chemotherapy) did not improve PFS or OS vs comparator and showed higher treatment-related mortality.

**Title:** Osimertinib plus datopotamab deruxtecan in patients with EGFR-mutated advanced NSCLC after progression on first-line osimertinib: ORCHARD

**Journal:** Annals of Oncology

**Date:** June 2026

**PMID:** 41780641 | **DOI:** 10.1016/j.annonc.2026.02.014 | **NCT:** NCT03944772

**Disease/setting/line:** EGFR-mutated advanced NSCLC with progressive disease on first-line osimertinib; second-line combination therapy

**Phase:** Phase II

**Design:** Open-label, multicenter platform study; two cohorts (osimertinib 80 mg daily + Dato-DXd 4 mg/kg vs 6 mg/kg IV every 3 weeks)

**N enrolled:** 69 (35 in 4 mg/kg cohort; 34 in 6 mg/kg cohort)

**Population/key eligibility:** EGFR-mutated advanced NSCLC; progressive disease on first-line osimertinib

**Intervention vs comparator:** Osimertinib (80 mg once daily) plus datopotamab deruxtecan (4 or 6 mg/kg IV every 3 weeks) vs historical/single-arm cohorts

**Primary endpoint:** Investigator-assessed confirmed objective response rate (ORR) per RECIST v1.1
- 4 mg/kg cohort: 43% (80% CI 32–55%)
- 6 mg/kg cohort: 36% (80% CI 25–49%)

**Key secondary endpoints:**
- **Progression-free survival (PFS):**
  - 4 mg/kg: median 9.5 months (95% CI 7.2–9.8 months)
  - 6 mg/kg: median 11.7 months (95% CI 8.3–21.7 months)
- **Duration of response (DoR):**
  - 4 mg/kg: median 6.3 months (95% CI 3.8–8.1 months)
  - 6 mg/kg: median 20.5 months (95% CI 6.2 months–not calculable; estimated median ≥16 months)
- **Overall survival (OS):**
  - 4 mg/kg: median 19.8 months (95% CI 13.5–23.3 months)
  - 6 mg/kg: median 26.2 months (95% CI 14.8 months–not calculable; estimated median ≥ 4 mg/kg cohort)
  - OS reported but median follow-up duration not stated; maturity not reported

**Safety (Grade ≥3 adverse events):**
- 4 mg/kg cohort: 49% grade ≥3 AEs; 23% dose reduction; 3% adjudicated ILD/pneumonitis
- 6 mg/kg cohort: 76% grade ≥3 AEs; 59% dose reduction; 15% adjudicated ILD/pneumonitis

**Conclusions:** Osimertinib plus Dato-DXd demonstrated clinical benefit; authors recommend 6 mg/kg as preferred dose despite higher toxicity frequency and severity, based on overall benefit-risk assessment. Safety profile consistent with individual drugs.

## Izalontamab brengitecan (Iza-bren; BL-B01D1) for EGFR-mutated NSCLC — pooled phase I/II analysis

**Journal** | Annals of Oncology  
**Publication Date** | 2026-06  
**PMID** | 41611210  
**DOI** | 10.1016/j.annonc.2026.01.009  
**NCT** | NCT05194982 (phase Ia/Ib); NCT05880706 (phase II)  

**Disease/Setting** | Advanced EGFR-mutated NSCLC; post-TKI progression  

**Study Design** | Pooled individual patient data from phase Ia/Ib dose-escalation/expansion (BL-B01D1-101) and phase II multicohort (BL-B01D1-203); open-label  

**N enrolled** | 171 total (data cut-off 30 June 2025); 121 at RP2D (2.5 mg/kg IV on days 1 and 8 every 3 weeks); 50 chemotherapy-naive post-TKI patients  

**Population** | Advanced EGFR-mutated NSCLC with disease progression on prior EGFR TKI therapy  

**Intervention** | Izalontamab brengitecan (bispecific antibody-drug conjugate targeting EGFR and HER3)  

**Primary endpoints (pooled population, N = 171):**
- Confirmed objective response rate (cORR): 47.4% [95% CI 39.7–55.1%]
- Disease control rate (DCR): 81.3% [95% CI 74.6–86.8%]
- Median duration of response: 8.5 months [95% CI 6.9–11.2 months]
- Median progression-free survival: 6.9 months [95% CI 5.5–9.6 months]
- Median overall survival: 24.8 months [95% CI 18.5 months to not reached]
- Median follow-up: 20.5 months

**Efficacy at RP2D (N = 121):**
- cORR: 48.8%
- DCR: 81.0%
- Median PFS: 6.9 months
- Median OS: 24.8 months

**Efficacy in chemotherapy-naive, post-TKI patients (N = 50):**
- cORR: 56.0%
- DCR: 90.0%
- Median DoR: 13.7 months
- Median PFS: 12.5 months
- Median OS: not reached

**Safety (N = 171):**
- Treatment-related adverse events: 98.8% (grade ≥3: 70.2%); predominantly hematologic
- Interstitial lung disease: 0.6% (all grade 1)
- Discontinuation for treatment-related adverse events: 1.2%
- Treatment-related deaths: 0 reported

**Authors' conclusion** | Hypothesis-generating pooled analysis showing promising antitumor activity and manageable safety profile; being evaluated in ongoing randomized trials.

**AENEAS2: Aumolertinib ± chemotherapy in EGFR-mutated advanced NSCLC (Phase III)**

## Elraglusib and chemotherapy in metastatic pancreatic ductal adenocarcinoma

**Journal:** Nature Medicine | **Date:** May 2026 | **PMID:** 41981308 | **DOI:** 10.1038/s41591-026-04327-4 | **NCT:** NCT03678883

**Disease/setting/line:** Metastatic pancreatic ductal adenocarcinoma (mPDAC), first-line, previously untreated.

**Phase/design/N:** Phase II, open-label, international, multicenter, randomized controlled trial. N = 233 enrolled (155 elraglusib + GnP; 78 GnP alone).

**Population/eligibility:** Previously untreated patients with mPDAC. Modified intention-to-treat population: 155 on elraglusib/GnP, 78 on GnP alone.

**Intervention vs comparator:**
- Intervention: Weekly elraglusib (GSK-3β inhibitor, 9-ING-41) + gemcitabine + nab-paclitaxel (GnP)
- Comparator: GnP alone

**Primary endpoint + result:**
- Median overall survival (OS): elraglusib/GnP 10.1 months vs GnP 7.2 months; HR 0.62 (95% CI 0.46–0.84); P = 0.01. Absolute difference: 2.9 months.
- 1-year survival rate: elraglusib/GnP 44.1% vs GnP 22.3%.

**Key secondary endpoints:**
- Safety: Most common grade ≥3 treatment-emergent adverse events (elraglusib/GnP vs GnP): neutropenia 52.3% vs 30.8%, anemia 25.2% vs 29.5%, fatigue 16.8% vs 5.1%. Overall safety profile reported as manageable.
- Explorative correlative analyses: Baseline circulating CXCL2 and TRAIL ligands associated with improved survival in elraglusib/GnP arm; increases in intratumoral cytotoxic immune cell populations observed.

**Data cutoff:** 27 April 2025.

**Next steps:** Phase 3 trial planned.

### POLAR (Phase II)

**Title:** Pembrolizumab and olaparib in homologous-recombination-deficient metastatic pancreatic cancer: the phase 2 POLAR trial

**Journal:** Nature Medicine | **Date:** May 2026 | **PMID:** 41882405 | **DOI:** 10.1038/s41591-026-04299-5 | **NCT:** NCT04666740

**Disease/Setting:** Metastatic pancreatic cancer (PC); biomarker-stratified (HRD status); maintenance therapy following platinum-based chemotherapy

**Phase/Design:** Phase II, multicenter, open-label; biomarker-stratified cohorts with two-stage design for cohort A

**N Enrolled:** 63 total (Cohort A: n=33; Cohort B: n=15; Cohort C: n=15)

**Population:** Metastatic PC post-platinum chemotherapy; stratified by homologous recombination deficiency status:
- Cohort A: BRCA1/BRCA2-mutated or PALB2-mutated HRD (n=33)
- Cohort B: Non-core HRD (n=15)
- Cohort C: Platinum-sensitive, HRD wild-type (n=15)

**Intervention:** Maintenance pembrolizumab + olaparib following platinum-based chemotherapy

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary Endpoints:**
- Cohort A co-primary endpoints: ≥43% RECIST ORR and ≥77% 6-month PFS rate
- **NOT MET** — ORR 35% (95% CI: 15–59%; n=20 RECIST-evaluable) vs target ≥43%; 6-month PFS rate 64% (95% CI: 49–82%; n=33 full cohort) vs target ≥77%

**Key Secondary/Exploratory Endpoints:**

**Cohort A (BRCA1/BRCA2/PALB2-mutated HRD):**
- Median follow-up: 37 months (95% CI: 27–47)
- Median PFS: 8.3 months (95% CI: 5.3–NR)
- Median OS: 28 months (95% CI: 12–NR)
- 2-year OS rate: 56% (95% CI: 41–76%)
- 3-year OS rate: 44% (95% CI: 28–69%)

**Cohort B (non-core HRD):**
- ORR: 8% (95% CI: 0–38%)
- Median PFS: 4.8 months (95% CI: 4.0–12)
- Median OS: 18 months (95% CI: 13–NR)

**Cohort C (platinum-sensitive, HRD wild-type):**
- ORR: 14% (95% CI: 2–43%)
- Median PFS: 3.3 months (95% CI: 1.9–4.8)
- Median OS: 10 months (95% CI: 8.9–24)

**Translational Findings:** Circulating tumor DNA response, increased tumor-infiltrating lymphocytes, and frameshift indel neoantigen enrichment associated with durable clinical benefit in responders.

## Gastric Cancer

### Guidelines

**Chinese Guidelines for HER2-Targeted Therapy in Gastric and Gastroesophageal Junction Adenocarcinoma (2025 Edition)**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Issuing body** | Chinese guideline panel (published in Journal of Hematology & Oncology) |
| **Disease** | Gastric and gastroesophageal junction adenocarcinoma (GC/GEJC) |
| **Version/date** | 2025 Edition; published 2026-May-08 |
| **PMID** | 42104480 |
| **DOI** | 10.1186/s13045-026-01804-8 |
| **Link** | https://doi.org/10.1186/s13045-026-01804-8 |

**Key updates vs. prior version:**
- Introduced refined HER2 classification system (four-tier: high, intermediate, low, absent) to redefine patient stratification for targeted therapy.
- Integrated standardized detection methods: immunohistochemistry (IHC), in situ hybridization (ISH), and liquid biopsy to address spatial-temporal heterogeneity.
- Systematically reviewed recent progress in HER2-targeted agents: monoclonal antibodies, antibody-drug conjugates (ADCs), tyrosine kinase inhibitors (TKIs), and bispecific antibodies.

**Strength of recommendations / level of evidence:**
Not reported (abstract does not specify evidence grades for individual recommendations).

**Note:** Full guideline text required to extract specific recommendation strengths and clinical evidence levels for each HER2-targeted agent class.

### Trials

### Phase III Randomized Controlled Trial
**Title:** Zanidatamab with and without Tislelizumab in HER2-Positive Gastroesophageal Cancer  
**Journal:** The New England Journal of Medicine  
**Date:** 2026-May-28  
**PMID:** 42202319  
**DOI:** 10.1056/NEJMoa2517729  
**NCT:** NCT05152147  

**Disease/Setting/Line:** HER2-positive advanced gastroesophageal adenocarcinoma, first-line therapy, untreated

**Design:** Open-label, phase 3, randomized 1:1:1 to three arms; multicenter

**N Enrolled:** 614 (302 zanidatamab-tislelizumab-chemotherapy; 304 zanidatamab-chemotherapy; 308 trastuzumab-chemotherapy)

**Population:** Previously untreated, centrally confirmed HER2-positive advanced gastroesophageal adenocarcinoma

**Interventions:**
- Arm 1: Zanidatamab + tislelizumab + chemotherapy
- Arm 2: Zanidatamab + chemotherapy  
- Arm 3 (comparator): Trastuzumab + chemotherapy

**Primary Endpoints:** Progression-free survival (PFS) and overall survival (OS)

**Key Results (median follow-up 25.9 months):**

*Progression-free survival:*
- Zanidatamab-tislelizumab-chemotherapy: median 12.4 months (HR 0.63; 95% CI 0.51–0.78 vs trastuzumab; P<0.001)
- Zanidatamab-chemotherapy: median 12.4 months (HR 0.65; 95% CI 0.52–0.81 vs trastuzumab; P<0.001)
- Trastuzumab-chemotherapy: median 8.1 months

*Overall survival (interim analysis):*
- Zanidatamab-tislelizumab-chemotherapy: median 26.4 months (HR 0.72; 95% CI 0.57–0.90 vs trastuzumab; P=0.004)
- Zanidatamab-chemotherapy: median 24.4 months (HR 0.80; 95% CI 0.64–1.01 vs trastuzumab; P=0.06) — **not statistically significant at interim**
- Trastuzumab-chemotherapy: median 19.2 months

**Safety (grade ≥3 adverse events):**
- Zanidatamab-tislelizumab-chemotherapy: 83.3%
- Zanidatamab-chemotherapy: 73.8%  
- Trastuzumab-chemotherapy: 74.5%
- Diarrhea (most common ≥3 AE): 24.8%, 20.0%, and 12.9% respectively

**Funding:** Jazz Pharmaceuticals and others

**Title:** First-line zolbetuximab plus mFOLFOX6 and nivolumab in unresectable CLDN18.2-positive gastric or gastroesophageal junction adenocarcinoma: a phase 2 trial

**Phase:** II (ILUSTRO study, cohorts 4A safety lead-in + 4B expansion)

**Design:** Open-label, single-arm; investigator-assessed per RECIST 1.1

**N enrolled:** 77 total (cohorts 4A + 4B); 71 in efficacy cohort 4B

**Population/Key eligibility:** 85.5% with CLDN18.2-high tumors

**Intervention:** Zolbetuximab (CLDN18.2-targeting monoclonal antibody) + mFOLFOX6 (5-fluorouracil, leucovorin, oxaliplatin) + nivolumab (PD-L1 inhibitor)

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

- **Cohort 4B, overall (n=71):** Median PFS 14.8 months (95% CI 8.3–not estimable)

- **Objective response rate, CLDN18.2-high (n=47):** 68.1% (95% CI 52.9–80.9)
- **Overall survival:** Not reported

**Safety (cohorts 4A + 4B, N=77):**
- Most common treatment-emergent adverse events: nausea (80.5%), decreased appetite (72.7%)

**Next steps:** Authors note efficacy and safety support randomized evaluation in the ongoing phase 3 LUCERNA study.

### CheckMate 649: Nivolumab + Chemotherapy, 5-Year Follow-Up in Advanced Gastric/GEJ Adenocarcinoma

**Date** | June 2026  
**PMID** | 41687718  
**DOI** | 10.1016/j.annonc.2026.02.003  

**Disease / Setting / Line** | Advanced, unresectable, or metastatic gastric, gastroesophageal junction, or esophageal adenocarcinoma; PD-L1 CPS ≥5 (primary analysis) and full ITT population; first-line treatment

**Design** | Randomized controlled trial, multicenter; blinded independent central review for response assessment  
**N Enrolled** | 1,581 (nivolumab + chemotherapy n = 789; chemotherapy n = 792)  

**Population** | Adults with previously untreated, non-HER2-positive, unresectable, advanced or metastatic gastroesophageal adenocarcinoma

**Primary Endpoints + Results** |
- **Overall survival (PD-L1 CPS ≥5):** HR 0.71 (95% CI 0.61–0.81); 5-year OS 16% vs 6%  
- **Progression-free survival (PD-L1 CPS ≥5):** HR 0.71 (95% CI 0.61–0.82); 5-year PFS 10% vs 6%  
- Primary endpoints met and reported previously (interim results); sustained at 5-year follow-up  

**Key Secondary Endpoints + Results** |
- **Objective response rate (blinded independent central review, PD-L1 CPS ≥5):** 58% (95% CI 54–62%) vs 46% (95% CI 42–50%)  
- **Median duration of response:** 8.5 months (95% CI 7.7–9.9) vs 6.9 months (95% CI 5.9–7.6)  
- **OS, PFS benefits maintained** in PD-L1 CPS ≥1, ≥10, and all randomized patients (subgroup results: not reported in abstract)  

**Safety** | Grade 3/4 treatment-related adverse events: 60% (nivolumab + chemotherapy) vs 45% (chemotherapy); no new safety concerns at 5-year follow-up  

**Minimum Follow-Up** | 60.1 months

## JCOG0603: Hepatectomy + mFOLFOX6 vs Hepatectomy Alone in Colorectal Liver Metastasis — Long-Term OS Results

**Journal** | Journal of Clinical Oncology  
**Date** | May 20, 2026  
**PMID** | 41564372  
**DOI** | 10.1200/JCO-25-01231  
**NCT** | not reported  

### Disease & Setting
Colorectal adenocarcinoma with liver-only metastasis (CRLM), resectable, adjuvant setting post-hepatectomy.

### Design
Randomized phase II/III trial, open-label, multicenter (JCOG).  
N = 300 enrolled (151 adjuvant mFOLFOX6; 149 hepatectomy alone).  
Enrollment period: March 2007–January 2019.  
Median follow-up: 7.7 years for disease-free surviving patients.

### Intervention vs Comparator
- **Intervention:** Hepatectomy followed by adjuvant mFOLFOX6
- **Comparator:** Hepatectomy alone

### Primary Endpoint
**Disease-free survival (DFS)**  
HR 0.72 (95% CI, 0.54–0.97), p < 0.05 (inferred from CI not crossing unity).  
5-year DFS: 49.7% (95% CI, 41.5–57.3) vs 40.5% (95% CI, 32.5–48.3).  
*Result*: Adjuvant mFOLFOX6 reduced recurrence.

### Key Secondary Endpoint
**Overall survival (OS)**  
HR 1.07 (95% CI, 0.73–1.57) — **did not meet statistical significance** (CI crosses unity).  
5-year OS: 73.4% (95% CI, 65.5–79.7) vs 80.1% (95% CI, 72.6–85.7).  
7-year OS: 69.4% (95% CI, 61.2–76.2) vs 72.4% (95% CI, 64.2–79.1).  
Deaths: 54/151 (35.8%) in adjuvant arm vs 51/149 (34.2%) in surgery-alone arm.  
Toxicity: 1 possible treatment-related death in adjuvant arm; 1 post-protocol complication death in surgery-alone arm.

### Interpretation
Adjuvant mFOLFOX6 delayed recurrence (improved DFS) but did not translate to long-term OS improvement. The authors conclude adjuvant chemotherapy may delay recurrence but does not improve long-term survival in resectable CRLM.

|-------|-------|
| Title | Pembrolizumab Monotherapy in Sorafenib-Treated and Treatment-Naïve Advanced Hepatocellular Carcinoma: Long-Term Follow-up of the Open-Label, Phase II KEYNOTE-224 Study |
| Journal | Clinical Cancer Research |
| Date | 2026-May-15 |
| PMID | 41770235 |
| DOI | 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-3528 |
| Disease/Setting | Advanced HCC; sorafenib-treated (cohort 1, n=104) vs treatment-naïve (cohort 2, n=51) |
| Phase | Phase II |
| Design | Open-label, multicenter; primary endpoint ORR by RECIST v1.1 per blinded independent central review |
| Intervention | Pembrolizumab 200 mg IV every 3 weeks for ≤35 cycles |
| Comparator | None (single-arm) |
| **Primary endpoint (ORR)** | not reported in abstract |
| **OS (cohort 1)** | Median 13.2 months [95% CI 9.7–15.3]; 24-month OS 31%, 48-month OS 17% |
| **OS (cohort 2)** | Median 16.9 months [95% CI 8.3–23.1]; 24-month OS 34%, 48-month OS 20% |
| **PFS (cohort 1)** | Median 4.9 months [95% CI 3.5–7] |
| **PFS (cohort 2)** | Median 4.3 months [95% CI 2.1–7.8] |
| **Safety (cohort 1)** | Treatment-related AEs in 73.1% (76/104); grade 3–5 in 26% (27/104) |
| **Safety (cohort 2)** | Treatment-related AEs in 54.9% (28/51); grade 3–5 in 15.7% (8/51) |
| Follow-up duration | Cohort 1: median 83 months [range 79.3–87.3]; Cohort 2: median 58.8 months [range 55.3–60.8] |
| **Key note** | Long-term durability demonstrated; OS effects sustained beyond 48 months in some participants despite ≤2 years of study treatment |


**Title:** Continuation of First-Line Systemic Therapy with Progression-Directed Radiotherapy in Patients with Oligoprogressive Hepatocellular Carcinoma: A Multicenter, Single-Arm, Phase II Trial.

**Journal/Source:** Clinical Cancer Research (official journal of the American Association for Cancer Research)

**Date:** 2026-07-01

**PMID:** 42126314

**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-4502

**NCT:** not reported

**Disease/Setting/Line of Therapy:** Hepatocellular carcinoma; oligoprogressive disease during first-line systemic therapy

**Phase:** Phase II

**Design:** Multicenter, single-arm (no comparator). Patients with oligoprogressive HCC on first-line systemic therapy received progression-directed radiotherapy (PDRT) with biologically effective dose ≥60 Gy while continuing first-line systemic therapy.

**N Enrolled:** 36 patients (enrollment March 2024–May 2025 from 10 cancer centers)

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Patients who developed oligoprogressive HCC during first-line systemic therapy

**Intervention:** Continuation of first-line systemic therapy + progression-directed radiotherapy (BED ≥60 Gy)

**Comparator:** None (single-arm)

**Primary Endpoint & Result:**
- Progression-free survival (PFS) — median 7.0 months (95% CI 4.9–9.7)
- 3-, 6-, 9-month PFS rates: 73.7%, 64%, 38.8%, respectively

**Key Secondary Endpoints & Results:**
- **Overall survival:** Median OS not reached; 1-year OS rate 86.4%
- **Objective response rate (ORR):** 64.7%
- **Disease control rate (DCR):** 98.0%
- **Duration of response (DOR):** Median not reached; 3-, 6-, 9-month DOR rates 84.6%, 79.6%, 70.8%, respectively
- **Quality of life:** Generally stable; transient increases in fatigue and pain 1 month post-PDRT
- **Toxicity:** RT-related adverse events in 16/36 patients (44.4%); mostly grades 1–2; grade ≥3 in 4 patients (11.1%)

**Prognostic Factors Identified:** Type of first-line systemic therapy and albumin-bilirubin (ALBI) grade at oligoprogression were independently associated with PFS.

**Follow-up Median:** 10.9 months

## Colorectal Cancer

### Guidelines

**Colorectal cancer screening: An update to the American Cancer Society guideline, 2026**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Issuing body | American Cancer Society (ACS) |
| Disease | Colorectal cancer (CRC) screening |
| Version/Date | 2026 |
| PMID | 42200680 |
| DOI | 10.3322/caac.70083 |
| Journal | CA: a cancer journal for clinicians |

**Key changes vs. prior version (2018):**
- Reaffirms initiation age of 45 years for average-risk adults; continuation through age 75 years (if life expectancy >10 years).
- **New screening options now recommended:**
  - Multitarget stool RNA test (mt-sRNA): high sensitivity for CRC; moderate sensitivity for advanced precancerous lesions; recommended at 3-year intervals.
  - Next-generation multitarget stool DNA test (mt-sDNA): high sensitivity for CRC; moderate sensitivity for advanced precancerous lesions; recommended at 3-year intervals.
  - Blood-based cell-free DNA assay: demonstrated *lower* sensitivity for advanced precancerous lesions and stage I cancers compared with stool-based tests; modeling predicts less effectiveness in reducing CRC incidence and mortality. Recommended only for individuals who decline or do not complete preferred screening tests.
- Continues to recommend annual high-sensitivity fecal immunochemical tests (FIT) and high-sensitivity guaiac-based fecal occult blood tests (FOBT) as preferred stool-based options at 3-year intervals.
- Emphasizes multiple recommended options to support informed patient choice and improve participation.
- Requires timely colonoscopy follow-up (within 6 months, preferably) for any positive noncolonoscopy screening test.

**Strength/level of evidence:** Guideline based on targeted systematic evidence review and published modeling studies evaluating diagnostic performance of new molecular-based screening tests.

### Trials

**Title:** Postoperative Hepatic Arterial Infusion With Oxaliplatin After Surgery of Four or More Colorectal Liver Metastases: A Randomized Phase II Trial

**Journal/Source:** Journal of Clinical Oncology

**Date:** 2026-May-20

**PMID:** 42018958

**DOI:** 10.1200/JCO-25-01737

**NCT:** not reported

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Colorectal liver metastases (≥4); adjuvant setting post-curative-intent resection/ablation after preoperative IV chemotherapy

**Phase/Design:** Phase II, randomized (1:1), open-label. N enrolled = 99 (HAI group n=50, IV group n=49)

**Population/Key Eligibility:** ECOG 0–1; curative-intent resection or ablation of ≥4 colorectal liver metastases after preoperative IV chemotherapy

**Intervention vs Comparator:**
- HAI group: oxaliplatin via hepatic arterial infusion + IV LV5FU2 for ≥3 months
- IV group: oxaliplatin via IV infusion + IV LV5FU2 for ≥3 months

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**
- Hepatic recurrence-free survival (h-RFS)
- Median h-RFS: 25 months (95% CI 16–37) in HAI group vs 12 months (95% CI 8–19) in IV group
- HR 0.63 (95% CI 0.40–0.99); p-value not reported in abstract

**Key Secondary Endpoints + Results:**
- RFS: not reported in abstract
- OS: not reported as reached; median OS not stated
- Safety and feasibility: reported as "acceptable safety profile" but specific adverse event rates not provided in abstract

**Median Follow-up:** 59 months (IQR 45–71)

**Conclusion (per authors):** Adjuvant oxaliplatin HAI plus LV5FU2 improves h-RFS after curative-intent surgery of high-risk CRLM, with acceptable safety; supports further evaluation in phase III trial.

## Alliance N0147: Tissue-Free ctDNA in Stage III Colon Cancer Adjuvant Chemotherapy

**Journal/Source:** Journal of Clinical Oncology (JCO)  
**Publication Date:** 2026-May-20  
**PMID:** 41616224  
**DOI:** 10.1200/JCO-25-02086  
**NCT:** not reported  

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Stage III colorectal cancer, adjuvant setting, post-resection  

**Phase:** Phase III  
**Design:** Randomized controlled trial; FOLFOX (infusional fluorouracil/leucovorin/oxaliplatin) with or without cetuximab  
**N Enrolled:** 2,260 evaluable patients  

**Population:** Patients with resected stage III colon cancer eligible for adjuvant chemotherapy; plasma ctDNA sampled post-surgery, pre-adjuvant therapy  

**Intervention/Comparator:**  
- Tissue-free epigenomic ctDNA assay (Intervention: biomarker stratification)  
- Comparator: Standard FOLFOX ± cetuximab (not specified whether treatment assignment was adaptive based on ctDNA status)  

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**  
Not explicitly stated in abstract. Disease-free survival (DFS) and time to recurrence (TTR) evaluated; multivariable Cox models adjusted for covariates.  

**Key Findings:**  
- ctDNA-positive: 461/2,260 (20.4%)  
- ctDNA positivity associated with advanced T-/N-stage, high-grade histology, obstruction/perforation  
- Higher ctDNA burden, deficient mismatch repair (dMMR), and specific mutations defined poor prognostic subgroups among ctDNA-positive patients  
- "Robust and independent prognostic value" for ctDNA assay reported  

**Secondary Endpoints:** Disease-free survival (DFS), time to recurrence (TTR), overall survival (OS)  

**OS Status:** Not reported (abstract incomplete; OS follow-up status unknown)  

**Notes:** Abstract truncated mid-sentence in RESULTS section; full methods and hazard ratios/confidence intervals/p-values not provided in abstract. Tissue-free assay genotyping performed with 739-gene panel in ctDNA-positive patients.

## JCOG0603: Hepatectomy + mFOLFOX6 vs. Hepatectomy Alone for Colorectal Liver Metastasis — Long-Term OS Results

**Journal** | Journal of Clinical Oncology  
**Date** | 2026-May-20  
**PMID** | 41564372  
**DOI** | 10.1200/JCO-25-01231  
**NCT** | not reported  

**Disease/setting** | Colorectal adenocarcinoma with liver-only metastases, resectable, unlimited number of lesions  
**Line** | Adjuvant (post-hepatectomy)  

**Phase** | Phase II/III  
**Design** | Randomized controlled trial, multicenter; not stated whether blinded  
**N enrolled** | 300 (151 adjuvant mFOLFOX6; 149 hepatectomy alone); accrual March 2007–January 2019  

**Population** | Patients with colorectal adenocarcinoma and colorectal liver-only metastases (CRLM); unlimited number of liver metastases permitted; eligible for hepatectomy  

**Intervention** | Adjuvant mFOLFOX6 (5-fluorouracil, leucovorin, oxaliplatin) after hepatectomy  
**Comparator** | Hepatectomy alone  

**Primary endpoint** | Disease-free survival (DFS)  
**Primary result** | 5-year DFS: 49.7% (95% CI, 41.5–57.3) vs. 40.5% (95% CI, 32.5–48.3); HR 0.72 (95% CI, 0.54–0.97) — **favors adjuvant chemotherapy**  

**Secondary endpoint: Overall survival (OS)** | **Reported and mature**  
- Median follow-up: 7.7 years for disease-free surviving patients  
- 5-year OS: 73.4% (95% CI, 65.5–79.7) vs. 80.1% (95% CI, 72.6–85.7)  
- 7-year OS: 69.4% (95% CI, 61.2–76.2) vs. 72.4% (95% CI, 64.2–79.1)  
- HR 1.07 (95% CI, 0.73–1.57) — **no difference**  
- Deaths: 54/151 (35.8%) adjuvant arm vs. 51/149 (34.2%) hepatectomy-alone arm  
- Treatment-related mortality: 1 possible chemotherapy-related death in adjuvant arm; 1 post-protocol surgical complication death in control arm  

**Conclusion (as reported)** | Long-term OS did not differ with adjuvant mFOLFOX6 compared with hepatectomy alone in resectable CRLM. Adjuvant mFOLFOX6 may delay recurrence but did not improve long-term survival.

### Colorectal Cancer Screening – Incidence and Mortality

**Title:** Long-term effects of colonoscopy screening on colorectal cancer incidence and mortality: a multicountry, population-based randomised controlled trial.  
**Journal:** Lancet (London, England)  
**Publication Date:** 2026-May-09  
**PMID:** 42102826  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S0140-6736(26)00508-8  
**NCT:** NCT00883792  

**Disease/setting/line:** Colorectal cancer screening; population-based; primary prevention (asymptomatic adults aged 55–64 at enrolment).  

**Phase/design/N:** Phase III, multicountry population-based randomized controlled trial (1:2 allocation); N = 84,583 (28,217 screening, 56,366 no screening); intention-to-screen and per-protocol analyses reported.  

**Population/key eligibility:** Men and women aged 55–64 years at enrolment from Norway, Poland, and Sweden.  

**Intervention vs comparator:** Single colonoscopy screening at baseline vs no screening.  

**Primary endpoints + results:**  
- **Colorectal cancer incidence at 13 years:**  
  - Screening: 375/28,217 (1.46%)  
  - No screening: 912/56,366 (1.80%)  
  - Intention-to-screen RR 0.81 (95% CI 0.71–0.90)  
  - Per-protocol RR 0.55 (95% CI 0.33–0.81)  

- **Colorectal cancer mortality at 13 years:**  
  - Screening: 106/28,217 (0.41%)  
  - No screening: 236/56,366 (0.47%)  
  - Intention-to-screen RR 0.88 (95% CI 0.68–1.08)  
  - Per-protocol RR 0.70 (95% CI 0.26–1.25)  

**Key secondary/subgroup findings:**  
- Proximal colorectal cancer: RR 0.91 (95% CI 0.71–1.09)  
- Distal colorectal cancer: RR 0.79 (95% CI 0.65–0.89); interaction p < 0.0001  
- Men: RR 0.77 (95% CI 0.64–0.88); women: RR 0.87 (95% CI 0.70–1.02); interaction p < 0.0001  

**Interpretation (as stated):** One colonoscopy significantly reduced colorectal cancer incidence but not mortality over 13 years. Colorectal cancer mortality was lower in both groups than expected at trial design.  

**Funding:** Norwegian Research Council, Nordic Cancer Union, Norwegian Cancer Society, Health Fund of South-East Norway.

## CAVE-2 GOIM: Cetuximab rechallenge in molecularly selected mCRC

**Journal** | Annals of Oncology (ESMO official journal)  
**Date** | May 2026  
**PMID** | 41443411  
**DOI** | 10.1016/j.annonc.2025.12.014  
**NCT** | not reported  

**Disease / setting / line**  
Metastatic colorectal cancer (mCRC), RAS/BRAF wild-type, refractory (EGFR rechallenge setting)

**Phase | Design | N enrolled**  
Phase II, randomized, open-label, multicenter  
N = 156/328 screened randomized in 2:1 ratio

**Population / key eligibility**  
RAS/BRAF wild-type mCRC patients selected by baseline plasma ctDNA comprehensive genomic profiling (FoundationOne Liquid CDx); prior EGFR inhibitor therapy status: not reported

**Intervention vs. comparator**  
Arm A: cetuximab + avelumab (n=104)  
Arm B: cetuximab monotherapy (n=52)

**Primary endpoint (OS) + result**  
Median OS (mOS):  
- Arm A: 14.8 months (95% CI 12.1–18.3)  
- Arm B: 12.9 months (95% CI 11–not evaluable)  
- HR 1.00 (95% CI 0.65–1.52), P = 0.983  
**Result: no significant difference**

**Key secondary endpoints**  
Median progression-free survival (mPFS):  
- Arm A: 5.3 months (95% CI 4.3–6.0)  
- Arm B: 4.3 months (95% CI 3.5–5.5)  
- HR 0.78 (95% CI 0.55–1.10), P = 0.158  
**Result: no significant difference**

**Post-hoc exploratory subgroup: 'negative hyperselection'** (tumors without pathogenic variants in KRAS, NRAS, BRAF, EGFR-ECD, PIK3CA exon 20, MAP2K1, AKT1, MET, PTEN, ERBB2; n=124/156):  
mPFS: 5.35 vs. 3.65 months (HR 0.62, 95% CI 0.42–0.92, P = 0.017)  
mOS: 15.0 vs. 11.1 months (HR 0.61, 95% CI 0.39–0.97, P = 0.037)  
Objective response rate: not numerically reported but stated as "improved"  
**Result: statistically significant benefit in mPFS and OS in this subgroup**

**Conclusion (per abstract)**  
Addition of avelumab does not increase efficacy of cetuximab rechallenge. Liquid biopsy CGP identifies patients who may benefit from anti-EGFR rechallenge.

## RESET-C Trial — Neoadjuvant Pembrolizumab for Stage I-III dMMR Colon Cancer

### CAIRO6: Perioperative Systemic Therapy vs Surgery Alone for Resectable Colorectal Peritoneal-Only Metastases

**Journal** | The Lancet Oncology  
**Date** | July 2026  
**PMID** | 42372745  
**DOI** | 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00085-9  
**NCT** | not reported  

**Disease / Setting / Line** | Resectable peritoneal-only metastases from colorectal adenocarcinoma; treatment-naïve or ≥6 months since last systemic therapy  

**Phase | Design | N Enrolled** | Phase III | Randomised, open-label, multicentre (9 Dutch + 1 Belgian tertiary centres) | 358 enrolled; 351 modified intention-to-treat (173 perioperative systemic therapy, 178 surgery alone)  

**Population / Key Eligibility** | Age ≥18 years; WHO performance status 0–1; pathologically proven resectable peritoneal-only metastases of colorectal adenocarcinoma; stratified by prior systemic therapy, synchronous vs metachronous peritoneal metastases, peritoneal cancer index, and HIPEC regimen  

**Intervention vs Comparator** | **Perioperative systemic therapy + CRS-HIPEC:** neoadjuvant CAPOX (four 3-week cycles; oxaliplatin 130 mg/m² IV day 1, capecitabine 2000 mg/m²/day oral days 1–14), followed by cytoreductive surgery with hyperthermic intraperitoneal chemotherapy, then adjuvant CAPOX (four cycles) or FOLFIRI (investigator's choice). **Surgery alone:** upfront CRS-HIPEC (mitomycin C–based or oxaliplatin-based, investigator's choice)  

**Primary Endpoint + Result**  
**Overall survival** (median follow-up 41 months, IQR 21–62)  
- Perioperative systemic therapy: 44 months (95% CI 30–54)  
- Surgery alone: 39 months (95% CI 31–46)  
- **HR 0.85 (95% CI 0.62–1.15); p = 0.28** (not significant)  

**Key Secondary Endpoints — Safety**  
Major 90-day postoperative morbidity (Clavien-Dindo grade 3–4) in 292 patients who underwent macroscopic complete or near-complete CRS-HIPEC:  
- Perioperative systemic therapy: 49/138 (36%)  
- Surgery alone: 40/154 (26%)  
- Most common: intra-abdominal abscess (12% vs 10%), anastomotic leakage (9% vs 4%), fascia dehiscence (9% vs 4%)  
- 90-day postoperative mortality: 2/138 (1%) vs 1/154 (1%)  

Major systemic therapy-related toxicity (CTCAE grade 3–4) in 161 patients who started perioperative systemic therapy:  
- 92/161 (57%)  
- Most common: hypertension (8%), diarrhoea (7%), neutropenia (7%), thromboembolic events (6%)  
- Systemic therapy-related death: 1 (1%) — hyperglycaemia  

**Conclusion** (per abstract) | Perioperative systemic therapy cannot be recommended in all patients with resectable colorectal peritoneal-only metastases.  

**Funding** | Dutch Cancer Society, F Hoffmann-La Roche

| Field | Value |

| NCT | NCT00089193 |
| Disease / setting / line | Melanoma, resected high-risk, adjuvant setting |
| Phase | Phase II |
| Design | Multicenter randomized controlled trial, open-label |
| N enrolled | 121 eligible participants |
| Population / key eligibility | Patients with resected high-risk melanoma |
| Intervention | 12-peptide MHC class I-restricted vaccine (12MP) ± GM-CSF adjuvant, given at one or two vaccination sites (four arms total) |
| Comparator | Four treatment arms: 12MP one site (A), 12MP + GM-CSF one site (B), 12MP two sites (C), 12MP + GM-CSF two sites (D) |
| Primary endpoint + result | Immunogenicity (reported as powered endpoint; results not explicitly stated in abstract for immunogenicity itself) |
| Overall survival | Not reached as primary endpoint. Reported secondary outcome: trend to improved OS with two-site vaccination vs. one site (HR 0.64; 95% CI 0.39–1.06; p = 0.08). OS not significantly different by GM-CSF status. |
| Recurrence-free survival | Significantly improved with two-site vaccination vs. one site (HR 0.59; 95% CI 0.38–0.93; p = 0.02). RFS not significantly different by GM-CSF status. On landmark multivariable analysis, two-site vaccination was the only significant predictor of RFS (HR 0.55; 95% CI 0.34–0.88; p = 0.01) after adjusting for CD8+ T-cell response and other prognostic factors. |
| Median follow-up | 5.6 years |
| Key findings | Two-site vaccination associated with improved RFS and trend to improved OS; GM-CSF adjuvant did not provide benefit for RFS or OS. |


## Phase III Trial: IO102-IO103 + Pembrolizumab vs Pembrolizumab Alone in Advanced Melanoma

**Title:** IO102-IO103 immune-modulatory cancer vaccine and pembrolizumab in melanoma.

**Journal/Source:** Annals of Oncology (official journal of the European Society for Medical Oncology)

**Publication Date:** July 2026

**PMID:** 42025759 | **DOI:** 10.1016/j.annonc.2026.04.010 | **NCT:** not reported

---

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Untreated advanced melanoma, first-line therapy

**Phase:** III

**Design:** Open-label, randomized, multicenter. 1:1 allocation. Blinded independent central review for primary endpoint per RECIST v1.1.

**N Enrolled:** 407

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Advanced melanoma, anti-PD-1 naïve and previously treated; includes PD-L1-negative and PD-L1-positive tumors; BRAF-mutated and wild-type; elevated and normal lactate dehydrogenase.

**Intervention vs Comparator:**
- **Intervention:** IO102-IO103 (85 μg each, subcutaneous) + pembrolizumab 200 mg intravenously every 3 weeks for up to 2 years
- **Comparator:** Pembrolizumab 200 mg intravenously every 3 weeks alone for up to 2 years

---

**Primary Endpoint: Progression-Free Survival (PFS)**

- **IO102-IO103 + pembrolizumab:** median 19.4 months [95% CI 9.7 to not reached]
- **Pembrolizumab alone:** median 11.0 months [95% CI 6.0–14.8]
- **Hazard ratio (95% CI):** 0.77 (0.58–1.00)
- **P-value:** 0.0558
- **Statistical significance threshold:** P ≤ 0.045 (missed)
- **Overall survival:** not reported

---

**Key Secondary Endpoints & Subgroup Results:**

1. **PD-L1-negative tumors:**
   - Median PFS: 16.6 months (combination) vs 3.0 months (pembrolizumab alone)
   - HR (95% CI): 0.54 (0.35–0.85)

2. **Anti-PD-1 naïve patients:**
   - Median PFS: 24.8 months (combination) vs 11.0 months (pembrolizumab alone)
   - HR (95% CI): 0.74 (0.56–0.98)

3. **BRAF-mutated tumors:** longer PFS observed in combination arm (numeric data not explicitly reported)

4. **Elevated lactate dehydrogenase:** longer PFS observed in combination arm (numeric data not explicitly reported)

---

**Safety:**

- **Grade ≥3 treatment-related adverse events:** 14.5% (combination) vs 15.6% (pembrolizumab alone)
- **Serious adverse events:** 32.0% (combination) vs 32.3% (pembrolizumab alone)
- **Local vaccine-related injection site reactions:** 56.0% of patients, mostly grade 1/2
- **Conclusion:** No increase in frequency or severity of systemic adverse events in the vaccine arm

---

**Conclusion (per abstract):** IO102-IO103 plus pembrolizumab prolonged PFS compared with pembrolizumab alone in first-line advanced melanoma; however, the primary endpoint missed statistical significance. Well tolerated with no added significant systemic toxicity. Potential benefit suggested by combination approach.

## Prostate Cancer

### Guidelines

**Prostate Cancer Working Group 4 (PCWG4): Trial Design and Objectives for Patients With Prostate Cancer — Recommendations**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Issuing body** | International expert committee; Prostate Cancer Working Group 4 (PCWG4) |
| **Disease** | Advanced prostate cancer |
| **Version/Iteration** | PCWG4 (convened 2016–2025) |
| **Publication date** | May 2026 |
| **Journal/source** | *Journal of Clinical Oncology* |
| **PMID** | 41744290 |
| **DOI** | 10.1200/JCO-25-02834 |

**What changed vs prior version:**
PCWG4 redefines terminology and best practices for clinical trial conduct in advanced prostate cancer in light of evolving imaging (PET-focus), molecular phenotyping, genetic subtypes, and prognostic assessments. Key updates include:
- Redefinition of disease state terminology and previous therapy terminology in a patient-centric and androgen pathway modulation context.
- New recommendations for imaging criteria (emphasis on PET-defined disease).
- Updated guidance on eligibility criteria, response assessment, delay/prevent endpoints, and reassessment intervals.
- New recommendations on patient-reported outcome determination.
- Biomarker-based context-of-use guidance for intended indications to reflect patient benefit.
- Extension of guidance to earlier androgen pathway modulator-naïve/sensitive disease states.
- Emphasis on development of validated PET imaging and molecular/phenotypic criteria for patient risk stratification and outcome measurement.

**Strength / level of evidence:**
Not reported (consensus-based expert panel recommendations).

**Key recommendations (summary):**
Patient and tumor characterization, therapy development, and imaging criteria recommendations for advanced prostate cancer trial design, with emphasis on heterogeneous and diverse patient populations to optimize treatment benefits.

### Phase II: Talabostat + Pembrolizumab in Small Cell Neuroendocrine Prostate Cancer

**Journal for Immunotherapy of Cancer** | May 11, 2026 | PMID: 42114950 | DOI: 10.1136/jitc-2025-014242 | NCT: NCT03910660

**Disease & setting:** Small cell neuroendocrine prostate cancer (SCNC), de novo or treatment-emergent; ≥1 prior line of systemic therapy. Median 3 prior lines; 56% prior platinum, 53% prior taxane.

**Phase & design:** Phase II, open-label, single-arm (no comparator stated).

**N enrolled:** 34 patients; response-evaluable subset n=30; 21 (62%) with visceral metastases.

**Intervention:** Pembrolizumab 200 mg IV every 21 days + talabostat (BXCL701) oral: 0.2 mg twice daily week 1, then step up to 0.3 mg twice daily days 8–14 and days 1–14 of subsequent cycles.

**Primary endpoint & result:** Composite response rate (CRR). CRR 20% (95% CI 7.7%–38.6%, n=30). Objective response rate 13% (95% CI 3.8%–30.7%). Median duration of response 9.0 months.

**Key secondary endpoints:**
- Median radiographic progression-free survival: 2.1 months (95% CI 1.9–4.2)
- Median overall survival: 13.7 months (95% CI 7.0–unevaluable); 12-month OS rate 54.1% (95% CI 34.2%–70.3%)
- OS maturity and follow-up duration: not reported

**Biomarkers (post-hoc):** All responders had low tumor mutational burden and/or microsatellite stability. Baseline DPP9 tumor stromal expression associated with response.

**Safety:** Most frequent treatment-related adverse events (any grade): fatigue 41%, hypotension 29%, pruritus 24%, dizziness 21%, nausea 15%, diarrhea 15%.

**Conclusion per authors:** Preliminary anti-tumor activity demonstrated; further evaluation in a randomized study warranted.


**Post-hoc analysis of ARCHES and PROSPER phase III trials**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Title | Radiographic Progression With and Without Prostate-Specific Antigen Rise in Patients With Advanced Prostate Cancer Treated With Enzalutamide |
| Journal | Journal of Clinical Oncology |
| Publication date | 2026-05-10 |
| PMID | 41894648 |
| DOI | 10.1200/JCO-24-02829 |
| NCT identifiers | NCT02677896 (ARCHES); NCT02003924 (PROSPER) |
| Disease | Metastatic hormone-sensitive prostate cancer (mHSPC) and nonmetastatic castration-resistant prostate cancer (nmCRPC) |
| Study design | Post-hoc analysis of two phase III randomized controlled trials; N = 2,551 combined |
| Intervention | Enzalutamide plus androgen-deprivation therapy (ADT) |
| Comparator | ADT alone (ARCHES and PROSPER) or placebo plus ADT (PROSPER) |
| Primary analysis | Co-occurrence of radiographic progression (rPD) and PSA progression (PCWG2/3-defined) or PSA rise from baseline/nadir; Kaplan-Meier OS analysis |
| Key results — ARCHES (mHSPC, N=574 treated with enzalutamide+ADT) | • 3.5% had no PSA rise at radiographic progression; 8.5% did not meet PCWG PSA progression criteria. • Among 79 patients with rPD on enzalutamide+ADT: 25.3% had no PSA rise; 62.0% did not meet PSA progression criteria. • Comparator (ADT alone, N=188 with rPD): 7.4% had no PSA rise; 38.3% did not meet PSA progression criteria. |
| Key results — PROSPER (nmCRPC, N=933 treated with enzalutamide+ADT) | • 4.4% had no PSA rise at radiographic progression; 10.3% did not meet PCWG PSA progression criteria. • Among 187 patients with rPD on enzalutamide+ADT: 21.9% had no PSA rise; 51.3% did not meet PSA progression criteria. • Comparator (placebo+ADT, N=224 with rPD): 3.6% had no PSA rise; 18.8% did not meet PSA progression criteria. |
| Secondary findings | Liver metastases >5-fold higher in enzalutamide-treated patients with rPD vs control (sample size noted as small). Enzalutamide-treated patients with rPD ± PSA rise/progression had worse OS compared with no rPD. |
| OS reported? | Yes, but as a secondary/exploratory outcome in the context of rPD subgroups; not the primary endpoint of this analysis. |
| Conclusion | Frequent discordance between imaging progression and PSA changes during enzalutamide treatment in mHSPC and nmCRPC; poor prognosis associated with rPD despite absence of PSA changes; periodic imaging surveillance recommended. |
