### Single-Arm Phase II: Apalutamide + AAP + SBRT in Very High-Risk Prostate Cancer

**Title:** Apalutamide + Abiraterone Acetate plus Prednisone + Leuprolide with Stereotactic, Ultra-Hypofractionated Radiation in Very High-Risk Prostate Cancer: A Single-Arm, Phase 2 Study

**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Date:** 2026-05-01  
**PMID:** 41712259  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-3746  

**Disease/Setting:** Very high-risk localized prostate adenocarcinoma (NCCN criteria: ≥2 high-risk features including Gleason 8–10, PSA ≥20, ≥T3, or >4 cores with Gleason 8).

**Phase:** Phase II  
**Design:** Multi-institutional, single-arm, non-randomized  
**N:** 63 enrolled (August 2016–December 2022)

**Population:** Histologically confirmed adenocarcinoma; very high-risk by NCCN definition.

**Intervention:** 6 months of apalutamide + abiraterone acetate + leuprolide + prostate/seminal vesicle–directed ultra-hypofractionated SBRT.

**Comparator:** None (single-arm).

**Primary Endpoint:**  
3-year biochemical recurrence (BCR) rate by Phoenix criteria.  
- **Result:** 19% (prespecified superiority threshold: <10%; threshold not met)
- **BCR-free survival at 3 years:** 84.2% [95% CI, 75.6–93.7%]
- **Median follow-up:** 41 months (range 34–43)

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**  
- **3-year metastasis-free survival (MFS):** 93.6% [95% CI, 87.8–99.8%]
- **Deaths observed:** 0
- **PSA ≤0.2 ng/mL:** not reported
- **Median time to testosterone recovery >150 ng/dL:** 6 months (range 3–24 months)

**Safety & QoL:**  
No new safety signals. Significant QoL decline only in EPIC sexual subdomain at 12 months.

**Authors' Conclusion:**  
Well-tolerated regimen with limited QoL impact. Although BCR rates exceeded the superiority threshold, outcomes aligned with historic benchmarks, supporting further evaluation in prospective trials.

## STAMPEDE Platform: On-Treatment PSA and Overall Survival

**Journal:** The Lancet. Oncology  
**Date:** May 2026  
**PMID:** 42061373  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00066-5  
**NCT:** NCT00268476  

### Disease & Setting
Metastatic or very high-risk non-metastatic prostate adenocarcinoma; metastatic volume or lymph node status stratification.

### Study Design
**Phase:** III (post-hoc analysis)  
**Type:** Landmark analysis from five randomized phase III trials within the STAMPEDE platform  
**N enrolled:** 7,129 patients (4,438 metastatic, 2,691 non-metastatic); 2,211 with high-volume metastases, 1,033 lymph node positive  
**Blinding:** Not reported  
**Comparators:** Standard ADT vs ADT + docetaxel; ADT + docetaxel ± zoledronic acid; ADT + abiraterone ± enzalutamide; ADT + radiotherapy (metastatic only)

### Population & Eligibility
Patients with metastatic or very high-risk non-metastatic prostate adenocarcinoma enrolled to STAMPEDE platform trials between Oct 2005 and Sept 2016 at 126 hospitals/oncology centers in Switzerland and UK. Only patients with PSA value at landmark timepoint included in respective analyses.

### Intervention & Comparator
Post-hoc evaluation of associations between PSA nadir (measured at 6, 12, 24 weeks post-randomization) and overall survival outcomes. PSA categories: ≤0.2 ng/mL, >0.2–1.0 ng/mL, >1.0–3.0 ng/mL, >3.0 ng/mL.

### Primary Endpoint & Result
**Endpoint:** Association of on-treatment PSA categories with 96-month overall survival, stratified by metastatic volume (low vs high) or lymph node status (positive vs negative).  

**Key findings:**
- PSA ≤0.2 ng/mL at 24 weeks associated with strongest OS association
- Among metastatic patients treated with abiraterone ± enzalutamide and PSA ≤0.2 ng/mL at 24 weeks:
  - Low-volume metastatic disease: 96-month OS 64.1% (95% CI 57.8–69.8%)
  - High-volume metastatic disease: 96-month OS 44.6% (95% CI 37.1–51.9%)
- Non-metastatic, node-positive disease: 96-month OS 79.4% (95% CI 73.8–83.9%)
- Non-metastatic, node-negative disease: 96-month OS 82.8% (95% CI 78.7–86.1%)
- PSA ≤0.2 ng/mL at 6 or 12 weeks less frequently achieved but associated with equivalent survival to 24-week achievement

### Key Secondary Endpoints
Not reported as secondary endpoints; this is a post-hoc biomarker analysis with OS as outcome measure.

### Funding
Cancer Research UK, Prostate Cancer UK, UK Medical Research Council, John Black Charitable Foundation.

### ARANOTE: Darolutamide in mHSPC — Pain and QoL Secondary Analysis

**Title:** Pain and health-related quality-of-life outcomes with darolutamide in metastatic hormone-sensitive prostate cancer (ARANOTE): secondary and exploratory analyses of a multicentre, randomised, placebo-controlled, phase 3 trial.

**Journal:** The Lancet. Oncology

**Publication Date:** May 2026

**PMID:** 41969015

**DOI:** 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00014-8

**NCT Number:** NCT04736199

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Metastatic hormone-sensitive prostate cancer (mHSPC); first-line treatment (recurrent or de novo).

**Study Phase & Design:** Phase III, international, randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled, multicenter (133 centers, 15 countries).

**N Enrolled:** 669 patients: darolutamide n=446, placebo n=223 (2:1 randomization).

**Population:** Men ≥18 years, ECOG performance status 0–2, with recurrent or de novo mHSPC. Stratified by visceral metastases (yes/no) and prior local therapy (yes/no).

**Intervention vs. Comparator:**
- **Intervention:** Darolutamide 600 mg orally twice daily + investigator-choice ADT (LHRH agonist, antagonist, or orchiectomy).
- **Comparator:** Placebo + same ADT regimen.

**Primary Endpoint (reported previously):** Radiological progression-free survival — HR 0.54 (95% CI 0.41–0.71) in favor of darolutamide.

**Secondary Endpoint (reported here):**
- **Time to pain progression** (≥2-point increase in Brief Pain Inventory-Short Form worst pain score OR initiation of opioid for ≥7 days): HR 0.72 (95% CI 0.54–0.96) favoring darolutamide.

**Exploratory Endpoints (reported here):**
- **Time to deterioration of overall wellbeing** (≥10-point decrease in FACT-P total score): HR 0.76 (95% CI 0.61–0.94) favoring darolutamide.

**Overall Survival:** Not reported in this analysis.

**Median Follow-up:** Darolutamide group 22.8 months (IQR 12.3–27.4), placebo group 20.3 months (11.4–25.2).

**Safety (Grade 3–4 AEs):**
- Hypertension: darolutamide 4% (19/445), placebo 4% (8/221).
- Anaemia: darolutamide 3% (14), placebo 4% (8).
- AST increase: darolutamide 2% (10), placebo <1% (1).
- Serious adverse events: darolutamide 24% (105), placebo 24% (52).
- One treatment-related grade 5 event (death, not otherwise specified) reported in darolutamide group.

**Funding:** Bayer and Orion Pharma.

**Status:** Trial ongoing but no longer recruiting (as of publication date).

### EORTC 1333/PEACE-3: Enzalutamide + Radium-223 in mCRPC — Final OS Analysis

**Journal/Source:** Annals of Oncology  
**Publication Date:** May 2026  
**PMID:** 41763609  
**DOI:** 10.1016/j.annonc.2026.02.009  
**NCT:** not reported  

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Metastatic castration-resistant prostate cancer (mCRPC); first-line therapy  

**Phase/Design/N:** Phase III, randomized controlled trial, multicenter; N = 446 (enzalutamide alone n = 224; enzalutamide + Ra223 n = 222)  

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Patients with mCRPC; enrolled November 2015 to March 2023; bone-protecting agents (BPAs) became mandatory from March 2018 onward  

**Intervention vs Comparator:**  
- Intervention: Enzalutamide + six cycles of radium-223 (Ra223)  
- Comparator: Enzalutamide alone  

**Primary Endpoint + Result:**  
Radiological progression-free survival (rPFS)  
HR 0.71 [95% CI 0.57–0.89]; p-value not explicitly stated for primary endpoint in abstract  

**Key Secondary Endpoint — Overall Survival (OS):**  
Median follow-up 58 months; 317 reported deaths  
HR 0.76 [95% CI 0.60–0.96, p = 0.0096], reaching predefined significance threshold of p < 0.0248  
Median OS: enzalutamide arm 32.6 months [95% CI 29.3–38.2]; combination arm 38.2 months [95% CI 33.1–44.8]  

**Additional Efficacy/Safety:**  
Grade ≥3 treatment-emergent adverse events (TEAEs): 57.6% (enzalutamide) vs 69.3% (combination)  
Grade ≥3 treatment-related TEAEs: 18.8% vs 28.9%; most frequent: hypertension  

**Key Conclusion (per abstract):**  
Final analysis confirms enzalutamide + Ra223 significantly improved both rPFS and OS as first-line therapy for mCRPC versus enzalutamide alone. Co-administration of BPA required to reduce skeletal complications.

**CASCARA Phase II Study**

**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research | **Date:** 2026-06-15 | **PMID:** 41880596 | **DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-4823

**Disease/setting:** High-volume metastatic castration-sensitive prostate cancer (mCSPC); first-line systemic therapy

**Phase/design:** Phase II, single-arm, multicenter (8 sites)

**N enrolled:** 61

**Population:** Patients with high-volume mCSPC and ≤3 months prior ADT; median age 64 years; median baseline PSA 6.6 ng/mL (range 0.07–745.7); 73.3% Gleason grade group 5; 69.5% with ≥10 metastases; 19.6% with homologous recombination repair (HRR) mutation

**Intervention:** Six 21-day cycles of cabazitaxel 20 mg/m² and carboplatin AUC 4 with continuous ADT, followed by maintenance abiraterone 1,000 mg daily and prednisone 5 mg daily

**Comparator:** None

**Primary endpoint:** Proportion of patients free of PSA or radiographic progression at 12 months
- **Result:** PSA-PFS at 12 months: 84.6% [95% CI 72.5%–91.7%]

**Key secondary endpoints:**
- Complete PSA response (≤0.2 ng/mL): 66.7%
- Complete objective response: 30.7%
- Overall survival at 12 months: 94.8% [95% CI 84.7%–98.3%]
- Progression-free survival: not reported as separate from PSA-PFS

**Subgroup finding (HRR-mutated vs. wild-type; n=12 vs. n=49):**
- Complete PSA response: 33.3% vs. 70.3%
- PFS: HR 2.43 [95% CI 0.93–6.39]

**Safety:** Fatigue, nausea, diarrhea (grades/frequencies not reported in abstract)

**Conclusions (per authors):** Feasible, safe, and efficacious; warrant further study in larger randomized trials

**Evolution of AR and Non-AR Alterations in ctDNA of Patients with Metastatic Prostate Cancer Treated in the Phase III Alliance A031201 Trial**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | Clinical Cancer Research |
| Date | 2026-Jun-15 |
| PMID | 41587107 |
| DOI | 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-2779 |
| Disease/setting | Metastatic castration-resistant prostate cancer (mCRPC); first-line ARPI therapy |
| Phase | Phase III (Alliance A031201) |
| Design | Biomarker substdy: longitudinal ctDNA analysis of plasma samples at baseline and progression; parent trial was randomized (enzalutamide ± abiraterone) |
| N analyzed | 327 patients with paired baseline/progression samples |
| Population | mCRPC patients enrolled in phase III Alliance A031201 trial |
| Intervention | AR-ctDECT cell-free DNA sequencing assay profiling tumor-derived genomic alterations |
| Comparator | Stratification by radiographic progression-free survival (early vs delayed progressors) |
| **Primary findings** | **Baseline:** AR most frequently altered gene. **At progression:** elevated cfDNA levels, increased ctDNA positivity, AR copy-number gains and AR genomic structural rearrangements (AR-GSR) increased; copy-number losses of FANCA, POLD1, RAD54L, CDKN2A, ZNRF3, ETS2. AR extrachromosomal DNA signature enriched at progression, associated with AR-GSRs predicting truncation of AR ligand-binding domain. Delayed progressors showed preferential AR alterations; rapid progressors showed higher non-AR alterations. Exact p-values and hazard ratios not reported in abstract. |
| OS reported | Not reported |
| Key secondary / mechanistic endpoints | ctDNA alterations stratified by radiographic PFS extremes; AR-GSR patterns and extrachromosomal DNA signature |

**Study rationale:** Post-hoc biomarker analysis of the phase III Alliance A031201 trial identifying genomic mechanisms of ARPI resistance (enzalutamide ± abiraterone) using liquid biopsy.

### Aglatimagene besadenovec (CAN-2409) with radiotherapy for localized prostate cancer

**Journal** | The Lancet Oncology  
**Date** | June 2026  
**PMID** | 42225101  
**DOI** | 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00071-9  

**Disease / setting / line** | Intermediate or high-risk localized prostate cancer; first-line with curative intent EBRT

**Phase | Design | N** | Phase III, randomized, double-blind (for primary endpoint assessment), placebo-controlled, 2:1 allocation | N = 745 enrolled (aglatimagene + valacyclovir n=496; placebo + valacyclovir n=249)

**Population / key eligibility** | Age ≥18 years; intermediate or high-risk prostate cancer; eligible for EBRT; ECOG score 0–2; enrolled Feb 2012–Sept 2021 at 51 centers (26 community, 25 institutional/military) across USA and Puerto Rico. Demographic: 79% White (591/745), 16% Black (121/745).

**Intervention vs comparator** | Three courses of intraprostatic aglatimagene (5×10⁸ CFU per injection) plus oral valacyclovir (prodrug) during EBRT vs. placebo intraprostatic injections plus oral valacyclovir during EBRT. Both arms received standard external beam radiation.

**Primary endpoint + result** | Disease-free survival (DFS)  
Median DFS not reached (95% CI 121.78 to not reached) in aglatimagene + valacyclovir group vs. 86.1 months (IQR 29.7–143.0) in placebo + valacyclovir group.  
Hazard ratio 0.70 (95% CI 0.52–0.94); **p = 0.016**.  
Median follow-up: 50.7 months (IQR 35.2–63.3).

**Key secondary endpoints / OS status** | Overall survival: **not reported**. Safety was assessed; TEAEs grade ≥3 occurred in 8% aglatimagene (n=40/479) vs. 7% placebo (n=17/232). Most common TEAE grade ≥3: acute kidney injury (2% both arms). Serious adverse events: 6% aglatimagene vs. 7% placebo. Treatment-related serious adverse events: 2% both arms (aglatimagene: 4 AKI, 2 pyrexia, 1 influenza-like, 1 urinary retention; placebo: 4 AKI, 1 increased creatinine, 1 rash). No treatment-related deaths.

**Funding** | Candel Therapeutics and US National Institutes of Health.

**Clonal Hematopoiesis after 177Lu-PSMA-617 Radioligand Therapy in Prostate Cancer**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Journal | Clinical Cancer Research |
| Date | 2026-07-01 |
| PMID | 41649873 |
| DOI | 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-4001 |
| NCT | Not reported |
| Disease / setting / line | Metastatic castration-resistant prostate cancer (mCRPC), docetaxel-refractory |
| Phase | Phase II |
| Design | Randomized controlled trial; post-hoc correlative analysis of serial blood samples |
| N enrolled (baseline / paired samples) | 178 baseline; 107 paired baseline-progression (60 177Lu-PSMA-617; 47 cabazitaxel) |
| Population / key eligibility | Docetaxel-refractory mCRPC |
| Intervention | 177Lu-PSMA-617 radioligand therapy |
| Comparator | Cabazitaxel chemotherapy |
| Primary outcome | Treatment-emergent clonal hematopoiesis (CH) detected by error-corrected deep targeted sequencing at VAF ≥0.25% |
| **Primary result** | Treatment-emergent CH: 62% (37/60) after 177Lu-PSMA-617 vs. 40% (19/47) after cabazitaxel; P = 0.03. Odds ratio for any treatment-emergent CH: 3.2 (177Lu-PSMA-617 vs. cabazitaxel). |
| Key secondary endpoints | CH clone expansion frequency and magnitude; PPM1D mutation frequency; maximal CH VAF change per treatment cycle. PPM1D accounted for 42% (51/121) of 177Lu-PSMA-617-emergent mutations (OR 5.4 vs. cabazitaxel). CH clones expanded more frequently and to greater magnitude with 177Lu-PSMA-617 (70.9% vs. 29.5%; P = 7.5 × 10⁻⁵). Maximal CH VAF increased +2.9% per 177Lu-PSMA-617 cycle (P = 0.002). |
| OS reported? | No. Endpoint is clonal hematopoiesis (a precursor state); long-term progression to hematologic malignancy not reported. |
| Baseline CH prevalence | 77% (138/178); similar between arms. |
| Median follow-up interval | 29 weeks (177Lu-PSMA-617); 27 weeks (cabazitaxel). |

## ARTO Trial – Long-term Overall Survival Analysis

**Title:** SBRT plus abiraterone acetate and ADT versus abiraterone acetate and ADT in oligometastatic castrate-resistant prostate cancer (ARTO): long-term, unplanned overall survival analysis of an open-label, randomised, phase 2 trial.

**Journal/source:** The Lancet Oncology  
**Publication date:** July 2026  
**PMID:** 42372744  
**DOI:** 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00178-6  
**NCT:** NCT03449719

**Disease/setting/line:** Oligometastatic castrate-resistant prostate cancer (≤3 metastatic sites); no prior systemic therapy for metastatic CRPC

**Phase | Design | N enrolled:** Phase II | Open-label randomized controlled trial, multicenter (16 sites, Italy) | N=157 (control n=82, experimental n=75)

**Population/eligibility:**
- Age ≥18 years
- Histologically confirmed prostate adenocarcinoma
- Metastatic castrate-resistant prostate cancer
- ≤3 metastatic sites
- No prior systemic therapy for mCRPC
- Stratified by: treating center, ECOG performance status, number of metastases

**Intervention vs comparator:**
- **Experimental:** Androgen deprivation therapy + abiraterone acetate 1000 mg daily + SBRT to all metastatic sites (1–5 fractions, biologically effective dose ≥100 Gy)
- **Control:** Androgen deprivation therapy + abiraterone acetate 1000 mg daily

**Primary endpoint (reported previously):** 6-month biochemical response (PSA decrease ≥50% vs baseline) — met (result of primary endpoint not restated in this abstract)

**Overall survival (unplanned long-term follow-up, analysis subject of this report):**
- Median follow-up: 53 months (IQR 43–60)
- **Median OS, control group:** 50 months (95% CI 36–not reached)  
- **Median OS, experimental group:** not reached (95% CI 55–not reached)  
- **HR:** 0.55 (95% CI 0.33–0.92)  
- **p-value:** 0.021

**Key secondary findings:**
- Grade 3–4 adverse events: infectious complications (5 control vs 0 experimental); cardiovascular disorders (3 control vs 3 experimental)
- Treatment-related death: 1 in control group (myocardial failure)

**Funding:** Fondazione Radioterapia Oncologica (non-industry)

---

**Note on this analysis:** Primary endpoint was 6-month PSA response; the OS analysis presented here was unplanned and the power calculation for OS was updated post-hoc after the primary endpoint was met but before data unmasking. This represents a secondary post-hoc analysis of a phase II trial.

## Sarcomas

### Guidelines

**European guideline for imaging of primary paediatric and adult osteosarcoma and Ewing sarcoma: systematic review and joint statement by the FOSTER consortium, Euro Ewing Consortium, European Society of Paediatric Radiology, and the European Association of Nuclear Medicine.**

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Issuing bodies** | FOSTER consortium, Euro Ewing Consortium, European Society of Paediatric Radiology, European Association of Nuclear Medicine |
| **Disease(s)** | Osteosarcoma, Ewing sarcoma (paediatric and adult) |
| **Date** | July 2026 |
| **Journal** | The Lancet Oncology |
| **PMID** | 42372754 |
| **DOI** | 10.1016/S1470-2045(26)00141-5 |
| **Prior version / what changed** | No prior version stated; this is a de novo European consensus guideline on imaging standardisation |
| **Development method** | Systematic review (2026 studies identified; 13 met inclusion criteria) + expert consensus (36 multidisciplinary experts) following International Guideline Harmonization Group standards |
| **Key recommendations** | 32 consensus-based recommendations issued covering: optimal imaging modalities for diagnosis, staging, treatment-response evaluation, and post-therapy surveillance. Specific findings: evidence inconclusive for optimal modality to detect bone metastases; no validated metabolic imaging indices or MRI parameters consistently predict response or survival; data insufficient to define ideal post-treatment surveillance frequency |
| **Strength of evidence** | Mixed. Authors note substantial evidence gaps persist; guideline relies heavily on expert consensus where trial evidence is sparse |
| **Clinical significance** | Addresses a major evidence vacuum: prior absence of international consensus on imaging protocols for these sarcomas. Formalises current multidisciplinary practice and identifies research priorities. |


### Trials

## Phase II: Palbociclib + Retifanlimab in Advanced DDLPS

**Title** | Palbociclib plus retifanlimab in patients with advanced dedifferentiated liposarcoma  
**Journal** | Journal for Immunotherapy of Cancer  
**Date** | 2026-May-04  
**PMID** | 42082272  
**DOI** | 10.1136/jitc-2025-014346  
**NCT** | NCT04438824  

**Disease / Setting / Line** | Dedifferentiated liposarcoma (DDLPS); metastatic or unresectable; mix of treatment-naive (63%) and pre-treated  

**Phase / Design / N** | Phase II, non-randomized, open-label, single-arm; N = 30 enrolled and evaluable  

**Population / Eligibility** | Median age 61 years (range 36–81); 67% male; 63% treatment-naive; eligible if metastatic/unresectable DDLPS or expected to benefit from systemic therapy prior to surgery  

**Intervention** | Palbociclib 125 mg orally days 1–21 of 28-day cycle + retifanlimab 500 mg IV flat dose every 4 weeks  

**Comparator** | None (single-arm)  

**Primary Endpoint + Result** | Objective response rate (ORR) by RECIST v1.1: **20% (95% CI 8% to 39%)**  

**Key Secondary Endpoints + Results**  
- Clinical benefit rate: 53% (95% CI 34% to 72%)  
- Median progression-free survival: 4.8 months (95% CI 1.71 to 15.7)  
- Median overall survival: 27 months (95% CI 21.7 to not reached)  
- Median duration of response: 18.4 months (95% CI 9.4 months to NR)  
- **OS reported and follow-up ongoing (median 14.8 months).**  

**Safety** | Grade ≥3 treatment-related adverse events in 61% (n not specified); Grade 4 neutropenia in 1 patient; no Grade 5 events. Palbociclib and retifanlimab discontinued due to toxicity in 17% and 23% of patients, respectively.  

**Biomarker Findings** | Copy number alteration burden and JUN amplification identified as meriting further evaluation as potential biomarkers of resistance; tumor sequencing details not reported in abstract.

### Phase IB/II Trial: Doxorubicin + Durvalumab in Advanced Soft Tissue Sarcoma

**Journal** | Clinical Cancer Research  
**Publication date** | 2026-May-01  
**PMID** | 41649866  
**DOI** | 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-2633  
**NCT** | NCT03802071  

**Disease/setting/line** | Advanced (metastatic/recurrent) soft tissue sarcoma; anthracycline-naïve, PD-1/PD-L1 inhibitor-naïve

**Phase** | IB/II  
**Design** | Open-label, single-arm (no comparator arm); phase IB: dose escalation and safety; phase II: efficacy evaluation  
**N enrolled** | Phase IB: n=3 (no dose-limiting toxicities); Phase II: n=41 evaluable

**Population/key eligibility** | Patients with metastatic and/or recurrent soft tissue sarcoma not previously treated with anthracycline or PD-1/PD-L1 inhibitor

**Intervention** | Doxorubicin 75 mg/m² (recommended phase II dose) + durvalumab 1,500 mg IV once every 3 weeks, continued until documented disease progression or unacceptable toxicity

**Comparator** | None (single-arm design)

**Primary endpoint & result:**  
Objective response rate (ORR): 31.7% (95% CI not reported)  
- 1 complete response (2.4%)  
- 12 confirmed partial responses (29.3%)  
Out of 41 evaluable patients

**Key secondary endpoints & results:**  
- **Median progression-free survival (PFS):** 7.6 months (95% CI not reported)  
- **Median overall survival (OS):** 23.8 months (95% CI not reported)  
- **OS maturity/events:** not reported  

**Exploratory correlative analyses (prespecified):**  
- Absence of RTK-RAS pathway genetic alterations: HR 6.446 (95% CI 1.934–21.486; p=0.002) for longer PFS  
- High PD-1 expression: HR 0.214 (95% CI 0.071–0.649; p=0.006) for longer PFS  

**Treatment-related grade 3–4 adverse events:**  
- Neutropenia: n=23 (53.4%)  
- Thrombocytopenia: n=6 (13.9%)  
- Anemia: n=5 (11.6%)  
No dose-limiting toxicities in phase IB (n=3)

**Conclusion (per authors):** Doxorubicin plus durvalumab exhibited promising efficacy in advanced soft tissue sarcoma with acceptable toxicity profile.

**Title:** A Phase 2 Study of Eribulin in Patients with Metastatic Angiosarcoma and Epithelioid Hemangioendothelioma.  
**Journal:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Date:** 2026-06-01  
**PMID:** 41481257  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-3362  
**NCT:** not reported  

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Metastatic or recurrent angiosarcoma and epithelioid hemangioendothelioma (EHE); largely taxane-pretreated population (85% prior taxane exposure).  

**Phase/Design/N:** Phase II, single-arm (parallel studies pooled). N=29 total enrolled (23 angiosarcoma, 6 EHE).  

**Population/Key Eligibility:** Age >18 years with metastatic or recurrent angiosarcoma or EHE.  

**Intervention:** Eribulin 1.4 mg/m² on days 1 and 8 of a 21-day cycle, until progression or unacceptable toxicity.  

**Comparator:** None (single-arm).  

**Primary Endpoint & Result:**  
- **ORR (RECIST 1.1):**  
  - Angiosarcoma: 17% (not reported as exact denominator of responders)  
  - EHE: 33% (2/6)  
- **p-value:** not reported  
- **95% CI:** not reported  

**Key Secondary Endpoints & Results:**  
- Disease stability >6 months: 6/23 (26%) in angiosarcoma  
- Continued treatment >12 months: 2/6 in EHE  
- Time to progression ratio (TTP2/TTP1) ≥1.3: 5 patients  
- **Overall survival:** not reported  

**Safety:** Eribulin tolerability consistent with published data; specific toxicity grades/rates not reported in abstract.

### Trials

### Covalent FAPI Imaging-Guided Precision Surgery in Patients with Medullary Thyroid Carcinoma: A Phase II Clinical Trial

**Journal/Source:** Clinical Cancer Research  
**Publication Date:** 2026-May-01  
**PMID:** 42013308  
**DOI:** 10.1158/1078-0432.CCR-25-3970  
**NCT:** not reported  

**Disease/Setting/Line:** Medullary thyroid carcinoma (MTC); newly diagnosed and recurrent disease; surgical indication  

**Phase/Design:** Phase II, prospective, open-label  
N = 50 patients enrolled  
Stratified into three predefined arms:  
1. Newly diagnosed MTC, R0 resection (n = 19)  
2. Recurrent MTC, R0 resection (n = 15)  
3. Unresectable disease or distant metastasis (n = 16)  

**Intervention:** [68Ga]Ga-CTR-FAPI-30 positron emission tomography–computed tomography (PET-CT)-guided surgery  

**Comparator:** Conventional imaging (investigator-determined surgical approach, for accuracy comparison on 231 lesions with pathology gold-standard)  

**Primary Endpoint & Result:**  
Biochemical cure rate at 1 month postoperatively:  
- Arm 1 (newly diagnosed, R0): 84.2% [95% CI, 60.4%–96.6%]; P = 0.007 vs. historical data  
- Arm 2 (recurrent, R0): 46.7% [95% CI, 21.3%–73.4%]; P = 0.049 vs. historical data  
- Arm 3: not reported separately  

**Key Secondary Endpoints:**  
- **Diagnostic accuracy (231 lesions, pathology gold-standard):**  
  [68Ga]Ga-CTR-FAPI-30 vs. conventional imaging:  
  Accuracy 96.5% vs. 72.7%, P < 0.0001  
  Sensitivity 98.5% vs. 81.7%, P < 0.0001  
  Specificity 85.3% vs. 20.6%, P < 0.0001  

- **Surgical plan modification rate:**  
  46% of patients had plans modified based on [68Ga]Ga-CTR-FAPI-30 PET-CT; 91% of modifications were histopathologically justified  

- **Event-free survival:**  
  not reported (follow-up duration, events, or survival curves absent from abstract)  

**Overall Survival:** Not reported; long-term follow-up data not provided
